O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book that is behind the science of medicine, assembling its completion with its explanations and by my declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in vision that I would complete this with your treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is twisted and distorted in our region and all around it, if the science has perished and been lost, and nothing remains except for small descriptions in books of the ancients who have moved their hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this arose errors and weaknesses, and the intentions were closed, and the science was moved away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems that I made a mistake, the text is not provided. Please provide the text and I will be happy to translate it line-by-line into English as requested.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because of that reason no good masters of the hand are found in our time, the art of medicine is stretched.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who enters into this art to understand anatomy, as Galen says, in order to know the joint of the bones, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and joints, and the number of the bones, and the movement and stillness, and the cause of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates says that the nose is very small, and the ear is small as well; and similarly in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	And so, in the introduction of this book, I say that whoever is not well-versed in the things said here, will be careful to avoid error and not harm others; thus I have had many times more to deal with those who intervene in this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a fool of a physician who cut the abscess on a woman’s breast or neck, and cut her arteries as well; for that reason so much blood came out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another physician who treated a large stone in an old man, and he removed a piece of the bladder with it; and three days later, the man died inside his own house.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have often called for the treatment, and seen the patient's condition and the size of the wound, and I know well whether it will lead to death.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another physician who treated the duke of our land, who had broken his leg and contracted an infection, and with ignorance he tied the break to the wound so tightly that he wouldn't let it heal, and thus I ended it; and he commanded him not to untie it; and he stayed like this until the leg was completely swollen and the pain came to a point of death.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to untie his leg; and when I heard it had been dislocated, he was in a good state and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all corruption of the flesh was already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until all the members were completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And behold, another mirror that will destroy and enchant, and then inflame due to the evil power of its sign.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humors, does not deserve to be touched with iron unless there is no remedy available because what is corrupted can be extracted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And dearly sons, you are in need of knowing that the work done by hands is divided into two sections: namely, to know whether it has danger or fear in various dispositions; and I will show in each one of these books where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For what reason he is necessary to protect you, so that the physicians cannot speak ill of you. If you take up your arms in compassion, and take your sick lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that through God's grace you come to salvation and are praised; and leave the terrifying diseases of bad health; and put away your weapons of what makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Galen's says in some of his teachings: "Do not take care for any serious illness, lest you be called a fool physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are on fire cautery and cold medicine, and the chapters are ordered from head to feet; and about forms of ulcers, iron tools for cautery, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and ventilators and wounds, and extractions of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and the ordering of the head just like it was broken into pieces, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Also that we remember the work, it is necessary to say which quality of aid and nuisance each condition has.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and the nuisance are the longest words and subtle science, and the secret answers; and many wise men speak about them and agree on this point; and they caution us not to repeat these words too much, because they are lengthy.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery is universally beneficial for all humors or whatever the nature of them may be; and it is so to two kinds of humors: namely, hot with matter, and dry with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry humors that contain matter, some have said and claimed that cutting is great assistance; but the others said the opposite: that cutting is of no use to diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated with heat or cold; and it says that those who say the opposite are wrong: that cutting is great assistance to hot and dry diseases that come into the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you examine the body of a man and his moisture corresponds to the hot humor, you find the body frozen.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with these words.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And not even a single way can be entered without the one who has tested it, and who knows from long experience the cautery of burns, and the diversity of human constitutions, and the inclinations and causes of their diseases, and remedies and space for treatment; we have no doubt whatever about other constitutions, in the same way as in cold and moist maladies.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all wise men concur and agree on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that cautery is gathered from fire so it is one of the secrets of cures, and has more good effect than cauterization with hot medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire cautery, it is simple, and does not come from fire unless it is applied to the member that is burned, and does not affect another member unless it is named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medicines applied to one member can move to another in causing illness or healing, and by chance the fire may harm the patient due to its height and the subtlety of its substance, unless there is excessive flow.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experiment and through long service and study, which I have applied to the art, and it was on the verge of truth; and for that I make excuses for the length of my words, because I do not like to reveal the secret that is in fire, and its quality, how it cures bodily diseases, as the philosopher said while demonstrating.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, when they agree on what times should be made the cauterizations, and choose to pray for.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is beneficial in all times, because the evil that is stored beneath by the aid of cauterization; and itself, if the cauterizations are done for painful necessities and sharp wounds that cannot wait until greater mischief comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think that dear son, how the foolish people do; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and they say so; but it's not as they imagine, because cauterizations are not a medicine that changes the complexion, but dries out the humors that cause pain, and brings relief in a short time due to its value, and through the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	In case the disease occurs only once according to the patient's complexion and the nature of the disease and its virtues; and the superfluities are assembled in it by acquiring meats and similar things, unless you administer cautery on him when he has a little superfluity and moisture, just as cautery for teeth because of pain and the similar things, but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	Many people do not understand why cautery is called the backside of medicine, and it's just an illusion; but they don't believe that cautery is worth anything after medicine, their thoughts are false, and cautery is considered the backside of medicine because when we administer various types of treatments for no disease, they don't work, so then we administer cauterization, and it's valuable.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And then open well that cautery is good for the backside, not according to the foolish opinions of the doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with an iron instrument was more effective than one of gold, and they said that the fires were used only because of the quality of gold and its substance; and they said that the iron cauterizers do not cause rotting, but it is not true for me because I have proven it, and found that it is not true in some people; and cautery with gold is more effective than with iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And know that when you heat an iron instrument, you do not know whether it is hot from the color of gold, and as soon as it cools down; and if you heat it too much, they make it in the fire; and thus there are enough obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use fire cautery which we have used before on our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or your have ordered this chapter to deal with the lower part of the body first, because it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	the olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the head, and due to the cause of an illness called "soda", and due to many humors that flow from the joints and ears, and numerous headaches and pain in the teeth, and throat, and the same illnesses that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with medicine dissolving and mollifying the head, three times a day, according to what the virtues and the oil and the custom of the sick person can bear; and then rub the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged, and place your hands between his hands, and put his hands on some cloth; after placing the root of your palm above the root of his neck, between his two eyes; and when your fingers come to it, if it bleeds a bit, then take out the cautery which is called "olivare", because this is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put a new cloth on the patient, and make him sit cross-legged, and place your hands between his hands, then placing your fingers one by one in twisting motion; then lift your hand gently, and reward the patient if you see a little bone; and if not, continue with the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you before; after take some wool, and put it on the cloth with olive oil and soft cotton inside, and place it on the patient, and let him stay for three days; afterwards put a moist linen cloth in butter, and leave it there until the wound is healed; afterwards treat the wound of the joint which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until he is completely cured.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if they say the old men, that when longer the wound stays, the purging is more; and therefore it helps to bleed.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say any of these that one must strip the cauterize so much of the bone is burnt, and then put what is burnt with the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say another that one must cauterize so much, and push it as hard as you lower the bone just as large as a wooden dowel that women put in their stitches, because that way the humors come out loose; and one should strip the wound for a long time afterwards; after that one cures and binds.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem to me to be entirely good in all things, whether by fire or in some men where there is no fear; and it seems to me that one should leave alone; for the joints are weakened by repeated solutions of nature, as we testify in other parts of the body; and even when the joint of the sick person is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more salve and healing for me, therefore I use over this remedy.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of old time great pain of the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When all of the head comes to chronic pain and lasts a long time, the patient must use the medicines and pills called "cochie", and purgatives for the head, oils, and plasters; and if they are made the cautery that we have just mentioned, it does not benefit.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Be cautious if the head of the sick person is of great power and will not be too cold; then the cautery should be done as we have said before.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After doing the cautery on each of the corners of the head where the bone is, as we have said before, and doing the cautery called "vasselz"; and it is in this that you put ventouses; and oil your hand so that you do not see anything where the bone is: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of that later; and it is fitting that the cauteries of the corners should be more subtle than those of the eyelid of the head, which is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Instruct the patient to apply fire cautery to the head.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When there is sudden pain in one part of the head and the disease spreads to the eye, and the sinuses are purged with medicines that take time, and all the other treatments have not been effective; then apply fire cautery according to two methods, namely by hot medicine and by fever.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The fire cautery of hot medicine is such that you press a dose of alum onto the skin, and strip off the scab and apply again over the sinuses; then make an incision on the temple where the pain resides in this manner that you can put back the dose of alum under the skin; and when it has been applied so that the wound is tight and secured, leave it for 12 hours; then remove the dressing and treat with hot alum, and leave the wound open for 2 days or 3; then cover with a cloth soaked in butter until ulceration occurs.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment until it is healed; and if you see whether do this with any medicine burning that I have written or prescribed to treat medicine burning.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of what is this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a bell or has little bird beak and a small appearance; and you place on the painful spot, and hold your hand tight and turn the knife a little lightly, until the red part of the pain is burned; lift your hand that the artery does not burn, which is behind, and drain abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Instruct the patient to put cotton in the wound for three days; then put linen on top of it for three days; next put moistened cotton in butter, and cure the limb with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this inflammation with the cautery called "cultellare", hold the entire point, and be careful not to cover the artery in that inflammation which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of inflammation.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	As you cure inflammation as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not benefit from this, and seeing that cauteries beforehand mentioned about medicine and iron do not bring relief, then it is necessary to heat up the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and so apply a hot line of half a thumb's breadth on the limb, and lift your hand once, and strain yourself so that you do not cover the artery and that it does not return to its place; and be careful about the mandible which mutates when one eats, and let no nerve have regard except for numbness and spasms in the patient, and beware of the corruption of blood from the artery when it is cut, or when cutting comes great fear and also harm to that person who does not know how to deal with it, and who is inexperienced and has not been proven; and leave the wound to its own course; but I will tell you how to preserve health when the artery is cut, and I will show it to you in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	Instruct the patient if you see that this fire cautery does not suit the illness, and the patient suffers greatly, cauterize it in the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is sound; and if you see, administer the fire cautery which we have said or chapter of extracting an artery, with the fire cautery that has two cutlets; and this fire cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain from a frost bite
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When ear pain comes from a frost, and you have tried the soluble medicines and other cures which we have said in cutting, and the pains do not go away, then use this fire cautery which is called "poins", because it is like this:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After poking around the sick ear, or near the II parts where pain holds in both, and you're a little bit away from the root of the ear after marking it with an instrument, then mark X points between each ear; after treatment let them be healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that should be cured by cauterization alone, and it is of those that move with pus, just as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make a cauterization for symptoms that come from ecchymosis and pus from wounds.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this semblance of torture that is muffled by pus and purulent discharge, and swelling of the head and gargarism, then it should be cauterized with three cauteries: one in the root of the ear, and another a little away from the temple, and the third near the junction of the two lips; and apply the cautery to the healthy part, so that the direction of the ear is set straight above a little below the cornicle of the head, and another in the temple about as long as our finger; and leave the cautery there until the moistness of the wound be dried.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the appearance of the cautery that we have shown before, but it is a bit more subtle and it is necessary that the cuts be a bit larger; after the cure, let him be as I have said, until he is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it in this way, and he does not profit from it, and the patient has no fever, then do four cauteries: two on each of the two horns of the head, and one on the forehead, and one on the "vessel" as we have said before, and a cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and treat him as we have said before.
de litargie	Of lethargy.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this sickness it is necessary to give the patient large and flat pills, of millet or poppy seeds for the brain; after that, make him drink his head full of medicine, and put the poppy seed ointment on the occipital bone, which is written in the treatment of ointments; and this is the manner of cautery: if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy in this way, good; and if not, make III cauteries on the two middle fingers of the hand, each one at a depth of I [two] feet from the base of the neck, and leave space between each cautery I [two] gross; and cure as with others, and if you see more blisters, then apply to the patient; and let them suffer if they do not make I cautery in the middle. And when it is done, II others on either side of the two horns, and cure until healthy; and apply those which are called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the frost of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is to be understood that the head must be purified with salt and what we have previously said. After taking the head from the patient, then make cautery on the middle of the head and on each horn, and one at the back and three at the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers, and the disease is severe, then make IV cauteries on the spine of the neck. Let it be left so long as the heat of the cautery subsides, and lift your hand; after the cure, until he becomes healthy, and apply those which are called "olivare" that we have previously said.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy.
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should only use fire cautery on one who is flaccid, and it is advisable to first soften the brain with years and other treatments that we have said in the section where the patient has great suffering and illness from pain of medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer, then make gargling and mastication to soften the brain often with bones meat; after reposing the head in mid-position, and make fire cautery as we have said before, on the flesh of the face, and each corner; and if the patient suffers greatly, then make fire cautery as I told one who had paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine at the back and neck; and use olive oil according to the way that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, then they must perform the subtle fire cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are superfluities or corrupted moistures and great gout, then the fire cautery of parts we have said has paralyzed.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluities decline into melancholy, and the body of the patient is moistened, then give them something by which their intellects may be purified, according to what it is in front in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying the chief of the patient; after making a linen band well made, like a circle, if you put it on the chief; and the patient binds themselves crosswise, and they must be bound in all parts; then present the linen, and anoint with melted butter from old sheep's wool; and let the heat temperate so that it may be able to be poured into them, and let it cool inside the chief; and perform this on each patient once a week, with another good government, until they are cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see someone being cauterized while they are multiple pokes with more holes all over the cauterization.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This way of cauterizing also moistens the brain more, and then puts on a wet cloth in butter and gelatin fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eye
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye comes first from above by the signs I mentioned in division, then it begins and proceeds to do something medicinal for the patient, making him sweat or take a bath multiple times with water.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After he asks to look at his head, and makes cauterization on the middle of the head, and makes a second cauterization on both temples if there is any weakness in both eyes together, or if it is only one eye that has weakness; then he cuts all over the cautery every vein and artery under the wound, and does them long as the width of the temple; and warns him to beware of bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then he stains himself with too little power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incising carefully how to extract them; and never, at no time, is done cautery or hatterel beneath the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the eye's flesh
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or at the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside; and one sees that it is a superfluity cold and vaporous, then do the cautery as I said in the beginning, below the eye: cut off the eyebrow, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries beneath the two bones; and if there is more need, cauterize with great care under the eyelid.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Two wounds from inside the eye
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you have given the medicine according to what we said in division, and it does not benefit the patient, then give him three bitter medicines; after the king, and cut off his head, and do a fire cautery on the middle of the cautery olivary; and do two fire cauteries on the cautery called "clavilis" on the two sores, one lower than the shoulders; and beware of the artery that you do not cover.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of olive oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cautery with this cautery called "olivary".
de coi ci est li forme:	Because of which it is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see so make II cauteres on the II scars also long as the scar is; and do not leave the hand apart except until the third part of the paper is burned, as I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the single hair that points to oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	There is no occasion when the hairs of the oil are converted to fat, and prick at the oil, and then do cauteries according to two manners: that is to say by fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their birth, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then put the patient in a sound place; after that make on paper around the eyes a figure just like the seed of myrtle, and as it is the beginning of the signs of hair growth; then put moist cotton in lard and musk of persillion on the oil, then take up the cautery of this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure that you have drawn little by little several times, and the wound is healed at the right place; and the signs of health in the work are that you see the paper withdrawn, and the hairs raised towards the point of the oil; then lift your hand, and let it be thus for III days, then put moist cotton in butter until the eschar falls off; after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if this happens afterwards, when the hairs come in, and the skin is softened then resume the cautery on the same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are absent, cauterize them until the skin returns to its natural position, even and not pricked.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and even, then make a bandage in the shape of a leaf of myrtle; then take French soap and live chalk, one of each point, and grind them together well; and do it hastily if it does not cool down, then press on the form as if you had made it like a leaf of myrtle, and put paper over the eyes; and if the patient only has oil in their joint, so must you also apply it in both; and place cotton wool soaked in oil under the joint; and tie your own hand showing above the medicine, and press one point and move all the time that the patient feels mordication of the medicine, because he feels it just like from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if you owe money to the doctor.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the swelling has passed, if you lift the limb in a way that it is lifted again as it was before, whether by constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this is not so, then put again the medicine on the limb or if the medicine has not worked, until your work is even, and your eyes are straight; then apply cotton soaked in fat until the wounds heal, after taking care of the limb which is called "dyafenis" (and others), until it is sane.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you think it necessary that you guard well your work with great care, so that the medicine does not touch your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	If the paper becomes moist after, and the hair pricks in oil, then resume the medicine on that part which is softened by its own paper, just as you did before; after the cure until it is healed; and this is the form of applying fire to a soft myrrh.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And since the eyes of men are diverse in size and shape, and according to these so be your cautions; and do not be replied with the right way for those who have the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment for a fistula by fire cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula in the same way as we have told in the division of diseases, and your treatments are not profitable, then it is necessary that you apply fire cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in a healthy position; and tie the nurses' hands around his head so it does not move or fall off its place; after putting wet cotton on the oil or persillion juice, apply the cautery which is tied like a bird's beak, assembled as if they were one piece; if you see, then point the cautery from one end of the neck to the other; and if you see, it should be so as if there was a tent; but this applies, this who has been tied values for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula until it opens up, and taking out the pus, and drying it; if it opens again, cut off the bowels; after putting on hot cautery in the shape of a beak, hold your hand to the cautery at the part not sensitive towards oil, so that you do not make madness; and put the cautery into the grease of the oil, and rot.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery procedure just after the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you do not come to the beginning of the cautery procedure just after the bone, then re-perform it once more, and if you have need to do so again, and let it lie for three days; afterwards put on a moist cotton cloth in butter, and let the cure with an antiseptic ointment until he is cured, and if forty days pass without his being cured, then put on medicine that corrodes the bone until the bone comes out; and do as advised according to what you will come upon in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a manner of cautery for an abscess that none of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Make sense of the abscess and sew it up; afterwards put in the wound a camel hair thread which is this shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it to the quantity of one pound of weight; and keep your hand firm over the canal firmly, and do not move the patient at all, until the weights sink into his body; and it is fitting that you put on the patient some moist cloth wet with wine or oil: the weight sinks deeply into the fistula, and the healthy person recovers marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, then it's good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, then it is fitting to administer poultices on the wound, and bring the fistula back to the body of the wounded one according to what seems good in his own sight.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Much of the time, cavities occur on lips that are called "poil", and at the same time in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When treating these cavities according to what we have said in previous chapters, and the treatment does not work, then use a small cauterizing knife with this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it immediately in those cavities until the juice comes out, after that treat with cerote as long as he is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the uvula, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has become rotten and dried up and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not work: then it is necessary to have a cauterizing knife according to the size of the fistula; after draining and closing the fistula, hold your hand until the iron awl comes out at the end, and do so once or twice, after the treatment as we have said, until he is healthy; and if it is cured thus, this is good; but if not, then it is necessary to discover the root and extract the rotting bone, according to what you will find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	Any movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, if you cure them with medicines, but that doesn't work, then put the head of the patient on a healthy bed; after scalding with cauterization, where the shape comes from afterwards in this manner that you place a cane on the tooth; and put hot cauterization in there very carefully, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after let go your hand and continue the cauterization according to your will; after fill the patient's mouth with a salty solution, and leave it for an hour and rich fires.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the teeth that were moving become fixed, and the gums are restrained, and the moisture is corrupted and dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pains of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain of the teeth comes from coldness, or if there is coldness in the vein, and medical remedies do not help, then it must be necessary to cut according to two ways: and fire cautery and butter cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter is done thus: you take butter from the milk, and put it on a iron or tin spoon; after putting cotton around the point of a tent, and applying the butter on the painful tooth, hold it until it cools down; and so do this many times until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth; and if you see that the molten butter and cotton burn, put on the aching tooth again, and place iron hot above the tooth until the fire comes to an end at the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Instruct the patient to take an iron or linen cord, and hold a chain of such size that it will not come near the mouth of the sick person; after heating, the form will appear afterwards, and place it on the tooth and keep your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be stayed on the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the sick person fills their mouth with good butter in the pressing of this cautery, and then the fat will come forward; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery on the head whatever you like, and according to what power you have; and this is the form of the chain:
des scrophules	of swellings.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are of mucus and cold moisture, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then apply heat to the cauterized head of hair so that it may follow afterwards; and have two openings for the fumes to emerge from the cautery on the other side; and put the cautery hot above the abscess once, or until it comes to a boil; and if the abscess is small, then apply cautery according to its quantity, and let it be so for three days; and place cotton wet in butter over the wound until it heals; after treatment with ointments and poultices until it is sane.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the snare:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture prevails on the channels of the gall bladder, and particularly when it comes from cold complexion, then it is fitting that patients be voided first by medicines soluble; after, apply cautery to the root of the throat, and take care not to come near the throat again, but rather burn only a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to perform the fire cautery at the joint of the neck and head of the spine, as we have the shape "clavicle" before, and treat him in the same way until he is healed.
de la toust	from the touch
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all the diseases of the phlegm are caused by cold and damp, and the patient does not have fever or sweating, and it is an old disease, then perform two fire cauteries on the liver in their veins; and a second cauterization on the area between the two breasts; and cut off the "clavicle" according to the shape we previously mentioned.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see that, perform the fire cauterization by pricking on all of the pointed part called "points" because its shape is as we previously mentioned in the disease of the ears; and make cuts at a distance of just thirty or forty.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment according to what has been said, and if the cautery is applied three times as described:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because that makes the cautery lighter, because you do it three times in one go.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After this, apply the patient on his back and on his chest; after lift the wound that is inside the titillite with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, then apply the cautery which has two nerves of the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	Instruct the cautery so that it cuts to the vein just at this cost, and comes out with the fugure of the cautery, four times; for this is made cautery with the three-nerved cautery, because the figures of cautery are these four cauteries; and they are nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and it is the form of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And at times, press against this nerve because there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After put the cautery on pearl-colored powder with silk; after make the patient rest, and do not let the limbs be long exposed for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if the dislocation occurs above, this happens little, therefore make cautery on thick corded cautery, or many cauteries in piercing.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	The joint is closed, and the moisture has been removed and the wound has healed for the patient.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When frostbites come into the stomach and there is a lot of moisture, and they are removed to their condition, and there are many purging movements for him, and such accustomed treatments, he does not benefit from them, therefore it is wise that the patient should be placed on his back, and stretch out his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After the third fire treatment, one cautery on the lower part of the nose with a spoon, by the quantity of two measures, all over the cautery hammer, and two more cauteries outside the two sides so that the figure of the cauteries is at three angles, and has the space between them equal to the space where they can be joined together when they will rot, and the cauteries are so deep that they pierce both parts of the flesh, and the figure of the cauteries according to this form so that they are adjacent.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	If you heat with great cautery in the belly according to this form; and if he has fear of this cautery, cautery in piercing and mark on the belly at that point according to the quantity you see of the needle; then the cautery should be done all over the thing called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment we had before, until it is safe.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver hurts from heat and moisture and great ventosity, so that it is forced to change its natural composition by superfluous things; and the patients are cured of what we have said in divisions, but they do not benefit, if it suits that the patient be put under his heat; and sign of the needle III cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, excluding ypocondros, at the time when the cold comes out from here; and there should be space between each cautery the growth of a doe; and the cauteries should be done long along the body, and not press too hard; and let only the moist parts of the kiss burn, and the patient should be turned right on his feet; and if he cannot, so let him sit, and extend his legs, and lift his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If your wish is, then cauterize these cauteries of the cutlery, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn all the flesh, because you would dry up all the body; and it will come to boil, for the flesh is very subtle at that point, and its wisdom allows one to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you see whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain that is not too great; but if it is in the membrane, he feels a severe pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure wants to drain the humors, it is advisable that the patient be supercharged on his head; and then he digs into the liver where the abscess is, and then heats the cauterizing instrument which has a shape similar to that of the bone.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Instruct the patient to cauterize as much as possible until the skin is dry and the wound comes out, so that the burn may be completely gone; after the treatment according to the treatment of the wounds, until they are healed; and it's not wise to use any fire from this cautery except for those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these illnesses have been cured once.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And thus it can be done courageously; and to me it seems that wounds should not be left open.
dou cautere de pleuresin	How to cauterize for pleurisy.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleurisy one should cauterize with the roots of Aristolachia, and in this manner: take a long root of Aristolachia, the largest you can find, dry it, and make it as thick and as long as your arm; and coat it with oil, and hold it over the fire, and cauterize between the nipple and the neck, then a little more downward towards the chin; and cauterize between the fifth rib and the sixth, after a slight angle; and one cauterization on the belly, and another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two cauterizations along the lower ribs, on the side of the one that is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but make it as tight as if you were smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	Instruct any old man that no one uses the cautery of fire similar to shaving, and then they attach it with an iron rod between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and take away the fires so much pain as we have said in the abdomen of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work is great fear or the patient will die now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	from the mouse.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.
