When you cure the disease of the mouse according to what we have said about divisions of treatment, and it does not benefit, then there are three methods of cautery that all are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one there is a method where you do three cauterizations, or four, in the same manner as we have said regarding the divisions of treatment, according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver that we have said before; and do not press your hand at all with the cautery, and let the patient rest on his back; and another method of cautery is such that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the wound where the mouse is, or when the symptoms come towards the left side, and lift the wound according to the wound, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries are according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Instruct the patient to heat two nails until they are perceived by the other side; and then burn the cautery, and so in four times will have done this. And if you see that, cauterize all of the cautery in three nails.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has been ten years since he got infestation by long vermin, and this is said to be equal to the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 cautery is not useful for dropsy, except when done in the way called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the ways we have told in divisions, and your cure does not bring benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries inside the wound, and one above the stomach, and one above the liver, and one above the mouse, and two behind the back over the spine, and one towards the hip; and let the cauteries be well close to the spot where the pain is.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After letting the fire cautery heal for a long time, and not relaxing the patient after the cautery; and recovery would hasten, and all two humors would be present with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the abdomen is like a hammer that we have shown before; and it is olive oil on the back, according to what has been put there beforehand.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet.
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical, and are filled with pus like citron, it is necessary to cautery on the back of the foot between the little and ring fingers; and lift your hand with the cautery turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And don’t enter too far into the marrow, lest it burn with the pus, and thus spoil the cautery according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even in each leg up to the point of the cutlery; and so hold the cautery on one long, one in front of the knee and another behind it, in the leg; and let the cauteries remain for a longer time until they bleed. After the cure of the other cures that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the house
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of stomach comes from cold and moisture, so that the digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are relaxed, and cannot be cured by any kind of cures; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with a strong verture, do thus: perform one grant cautery on the stomach according to what he has spoken before or the cautery for the stomach, at the cautery that circulates; and four cauteries subtle around the navel subtle, and two cauteries on the groin.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, let him be cauterized on the fingernail, and cauterize on each joint, and ask for cauteries on the stomach with the great one, because the treatment is advantageous when it has good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of treating hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are located at the fundament, or one or more of them, and they have been old for a while, and are large, cold, moist, and corrupted humors, and if treated as we have said in divisions, but it does not profit, then do cauteries: three on the spine of the back, which is located behind the navel, and a little to one side, in a triangular shape; and two on the buttock. And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and you see swelling on the face, then give one cautery on the stomach, as previously said, and one more on the liver, and one more on the mouse, with all the cauteries hammered; and let the cautery work for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment the limb will be sane once again.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is named "theleul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the fleshiness which is named "theleul", if it seems like a rasp, and then puts it entirely on fire above the part cut off; and let go of your hand while the cautery comes to life at the root of the vein, because the blood stops; do this once or twice, and if there is much fleshiness, cauterize each one as we have said; after the treatment with ointments, until it is sane again; and if you cauterize a great cautery on the flesh, it will give more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of a wound badly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear tightness or opening, which we will recount in his own words, if this illness comes upon him that he cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is an ulcer and it has become inflamed, and putrid matter and moist spots have corrupted it, if you prove to see all of its depth in a subtle tent, and guard that you know the extent of its depth.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After applying the cautery that seems like a razor, and pouring it into the ulcer according to the quantity that it has entered, and repeating the cautery until the rotten and corrupted flesh are burned, once or twice, depending on the amount of matter; and be careful not to irritate the nerves, and great pains.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	In case the fistula is in the course of the vulva and the intestine, if you observe these signs, and do not perform these procedures only on a charnel [corpse], think that they are not human; after cure, let him be treated until he is well, and if his limbs are diseased, and the materials are hardened for long time, then know that his limbs are completely cured; and if the materials are not hardened, know that his limbs are corrupted, and the bones are rotten to death; and in this manner, as one of these that we will say in his presence.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from a blow reaches the kidneys, and great swelling, and does not abate even in a woman, then it is proper to apply cautery on both sides of the kidneys, on one side with the flail-like cautery that we have previously mentioned; and if the cautery is applied at the center, if three applications are made in line, and they offer more aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and shriveled due to injury and moisture, if it retains urine, then he does cutting (cautery) in the part behind the bladder, where the hair follicles begin, both on the right and left side, and cuts each one as long as the nail; and he makes it cut behind the back, wherever he may need it; and cuts according to the shape previously said.
de la marris	of the gallbladder
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the gallbladder is cold and moist, and does not let it form because of this, and its flowers are corrupted and their endings are delayed; and when they come, he feels great pain: therefore it is necessary to make three cuts around the belly, as we have said for cutting of the bladder, and two cuts behind the back; and cut according to what we have said.
de la hainche	From the hair
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist urine descends to the flesh of the cheek and because of this, it is mute from its place, and it is found that the cheek is longer than the other when measured together; and it is marked by the leanness of the departure from the joint, so it is fitting that you cauterize the patient on the flesh of the cheek with a cautery like the circle, and mark in front of the joint as it turns, so that the cheek lies within the circle; and if it is cauterized like those who have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, do three cauterizations of the large olive tree, and make them as deep as all the other wounds; and care for the patient until they are healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin, and it's caused by cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division, but their cure does not work, and the illness is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of the great humors of fetid pills or other hard-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After cutting, and the method of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say by assembling hot medicines, and cautery with fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Cautery with fire is according to many manners, one of which is this: that you cauterize on the groin for three cauteries, and in this manner you make triangular cuts, of great depth and broad, and space them out so that there is a gap of the size of two fingers between each cautery, and use olive oil; sometimes it's done at the midpoint over the top of the groin, because there are four manners according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, so the fire cautery on the cut of the circle which we have said before in the dislocation of the hamstring; but do it in such a manner that the circle contains all the hamstring, and all the flesh around it be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way to do it in a sciatom (sciatic) treatment, when the pain lies in the hamstring, and does not reach as far as the thigh or the knee.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and the knee, if he does two fire cauteries in that place where the patient says the pain lies, and the first cautery on the ankle, one point to the left; and let the cautery be cutting (cutellaire), or let the thickness of the skin around the wound be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain is spreading up to two feet or almost to his knee, then cauterize at the place where he feels the pain three points or four.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	Instruct the master to do so if he wishes; and if it is done in this manner, when the pain is below the groin towards the thigh, perform fire cautery on the cutlery or circular cautery, and carefully guard yourself in all your cauteries that you do not burn the nerves and great arteries, and cause no greater nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen others who were cautered on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so that the leg was completely swollen, and the toes as well, and they became discolored and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a remedy for the stomach that caused his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in both sides together, perform cautery in one and the other, as this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	Instruct the wise men to use fire cautery on the hainche, for this is the method. Make such a iron and put it in the chief as big as an anchor of dactyl, or somewhat less, and make it between the teeth so that there is space between them from one end to the other by the length of a little finger; and let the spaces be equal on both sides, and also like nails, and have iron hands well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated so that it is completely red and has senteles (sulfur), and then put it on the armpit of the sick hainche, and turn it onto its healthy side; let cautery be applied once, and let it sit for three days; then apply ointment of butter, and let the wound remain uncovered for a long time; after the treatment of pain until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its sharpness, and if you see little who use it; and all hope that is good cautery, which he can bear, and in which he affirms.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burns if you make an instrument between crossbars, in which the edge descends down from the margin of the portal, and is made of iron or of fire a long appearance, and at high has two, and is between each one the quantity of the thickness of a pair; and is over and above, and they join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the ghee of hazelnut on the patient lying on his side along his coast, and press quickly your hand much above the ghee of hazelnut; after put in between the two circles of the hot awl which is heated a little, and he leaves one hour double tens, and suffer him the patient the heat and the inflammation of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For the mordication, it is true as for fire; and when the mordications do not pass, hold with your hand on the instrument and lift up the armpit of flesh, and let so three days, and apply butter until what is black from the ashes be extracted; and let him three days to rot in his strait, and that would be the rear aid after the treatment of ointments until he is healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended just to the thigh or just to the leg, then make an instrument that is held like the one I described in the armpit; and this is the way of hot water, and I have written it on treating the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alum and vinegar, equal amounts of each, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	If it has no small opening to prevent the point of a razor from entering; and cover that pot with another pot well filled with lead, and place above salt and chalk and water so, until you have two pots full of powder as soon as you take them in your hand; and leave it thus until it comes out blood and cheese or lead pot, then take all that and grieve over chalk and over salt as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And when it is very bloody and is being managed with the movement of old medicine and cauterization of other limbs; because all work done with fire, and with other medicines, where you cauterize well the vein as in this example and honey anacardi and chalk with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Galen tells us of a cure for one man who was cured of the pain in his thigh and sciatica, and praises it greatly, and says that no other cure is needed, and he became sane once, when this cure was done, and he bathed as he taught after this.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	Instruct the patient to press a fresh, green, and dry herb into the affected area, and pound it much with just a little fat, and place it on the groin and on the thigh where the pain is located, and bind; and let him lie for three hours and according to the quantity that the patient does not feel the pain anymore.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put it into a bath until the body is slightly swollen, and place him in bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And notice that no one should use cautery with these medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Galen says that when the varicose vein is cauterized with horse's tendon, if it helps a great deal; and in this manner must be done the cautery.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a linen cloth and anoint it with old oil, and put it on the depression that is between the little toe and the great toe which they call the fossicle.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dried cheese (meaning probably a medicinal herb like myrrh) and applying it to the flesh so that it burns into charcoal, anoint with linen and let it burn until it stains; repeat again so, and do not cease doing this until you think it has reached the point where the pain will be gone, and when it comes to the hunch of the spine, stop; and this kind of cautery is called "cautery of cheese".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or concussion or from excessive blood loss, or as if there is material spread out cold, none of these symptoms warrant cautery, except for that which arises from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after these that the patient be free from fetid pills or other similar things on his back, where the pain lies, three lines signed to burn with cautery, and in each line, either a cautery or more according to virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and the cautery shall be done as is called "poins"; and if you see, do III cauteries or IV at the cautery of the clavicle median according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow spine when they rise up, and fear; and you will find in the lower back of the spine on their back and in this appearance which appears on other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it being cured, if you cautery with the cautery of a cell according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery is applied to each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, when the fire is applied on the spine within two or three lines, and the points are close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the treatment of the patient as long as he is healed according to what we have said, and be careful that you do not apply fire in goutiness which is in pain of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by moisture that has spread to each limb of the body, and when the pain comes into the foot, which they call "podagre" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured with medicines, if it is cured by fire in this manner: make a poultice of fire on the joint of the foot, and use olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	If there is a sore where you must prick on the face of the foot, then do fire cautery to all the cautery that we claim "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	If the pains come just to the groin and other joints, and this happens often, do fire cautery on each knee III cauteries or IV of each part, all the olive oil cautery; and if you need more, do it again, but do not hold your hand in the fire longer than until the spice is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	If the pains descend just to the groin and on the back, follow the cautery we have discussed in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	If the pains are in the hands, prick 2 lines into the flesh; and if it does not stay sore afterward, prick again on each joint and on the skin of the hand; if pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and do good treatment for the patient with medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	If you do good governance and purge the flood, then you will be made whole by God.
de la routure dou syfac	From the surgery of the spleen.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the spleen is cut with pitch and the bile descends into the veins and it's new, you should wait until his wounds have healed before doing that again; and use things that ease his belly so that his bowels come down from his belly. After that, make him lie on his back between your hands, and tell him to tuck up his thigh as long as he can feel pain in it, and pull them tight to your fingers, and sign with a cut above the bone of the finger; then do the cautery according to this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	So long as he is white and his senses are clear.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then extract the bowels at their site; and let the physicians grasp his hand so it does not return to its place; and work well on the patient, putting a cloth and a servant over the knees, and another over the leg that grasps the hands; then put the cautery on the sign of all your fingers, your right hand and your thumb as long as you touch the bone, and if you do not touch the bone the first time, it will recur again for as long as you live until you have touched the bone; and be careful so that the bowels do not escape when you make the cautery; lest you burn them; and so that the patient may not die, or suffer another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	Instruct that cautery in children should be subtle according to the measure of each one, and of great men also great according to their measure; after three days cure him with burre cautery until the scar is removed; after the cure of other ointments until he is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days above his wound so that it is well covered; and it should be recommended to them to remain still long enough, so that the boil does not burst when they come to go in chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, give him a well-made bandage and tie it for forty other days; let him have good rest, that he works little and avoids excessive drinking of wine and eating, and speaking too loudly; and if you follow this teaching, he will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after the treatment of cutting on your chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the surgical incision of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When other incisions occur in the belly and are known, and you see that they do not grow again, perform the cautery treatment according to its quantity, and take one-third of the temperature; after this cure, as we have said. And none of the ancient ones said that it should be cauterized at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the shape of the wound with an incision and make a line for the width above the cut, and another one afterwards, and take hold of it all with your whole hand to apply the cautery knife.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cuts are lighter and less painful.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, from a fall or from an injury, and that pain lasts for a long time, and medicine cures are not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize with the cautery called "poins", and do the cauteries according to the length of the limb and its thinness and weakness and virtue and its location regarding twists and pains.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If there is healing from the first cauterization, that is good; if not, repeat the cauterization on the same spot, because it is customary to make the member move by its proximity, so that you should do the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of surgery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The trouble is not cured by cauterization with great help, and the disease itself that comes from the rot of worms and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You can see cauterization, take precautions if the disease is at the beginning, and cure it as we have said in the division, and do not insert or stay there, and doubt that corruption spreads throughout the whole patient, then cut cauterize on the head: I put new dressing on the head, and the other towards the front of the eyebrows; II on each horn, and I behind the neck, and let as long as your hand is free so that cauterization comes just to the bone, and until skin peels off so that vapor of big humors can come out; and cauterize on the flesh according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the malady is spread all over; and it manifests itself, so it is advisable to cauterize with those cauteries which we have said about in the head, and one cautery in the nostrils, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one on the groin, and another on the other spot, and two on the shoulders, and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the cavities of the hands; and beware not to burn those that are found under the skin calcifying, so as not to burn them; and never do a cautery on the bone of the finger, or another on the bone of the stomach, or another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And you know that when you do more cauterizations, the patient's recovery is greater, and they profit; and you know that the sick do not feel any pain in the cautery as much as they feel it when they are healthy, because the body is entirely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the fire cautery be great or small according to the limbs and joints, as you will find in different kinds of tools.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment, apply a mixture of flour and honey many times until he is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When an inflammation comes into any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it does not heal, then the fire cautery should be applied to the member according to its size and smallness; and if the cautery is inserted a little in the flesh where the pain is located; then the treatment of ointments until he heals.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes the cautery is done by hand and with a foot and on the back, at the end of the nerve that silences the member, and thus if it is withdrawn; and no one should get involved unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of leeches
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "leeches" is weakened, and the art of medicine offers nothing, then cut with cautery on one part of it, according to the quantity of the affected place, until the pus is drained off, and its color changes; then treat with a mixture of flour from wheat and lentils with olive oil and leaves of plantain, and salt of colon and salt of alondre, each in part; and mix everything together, bind it with a cloth, and apply to the patient as long as he is cured.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When chancre comes to the beginning, and your sight stops, cut with cautery around the circle that seems whole inside the turn of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all the wise men said that you should apply fire cautery at the center of a chancre; and all of them do not seem good to me, because I fear it will be ulcerous and corrupted, and I have seen no time that it would come to this; and there is no other more dire thing than being cauterized inwards, as the "circule" fire is called, just like we said about many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be killed
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some people have a disease called "adubelati", and it lingers in death or because of the overflowing that it makes, or because of the old age of the patient when he is decrepit (that means being very old) and has little blood, or because of time; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize it inwardly with many small cauteries, after that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	She will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced by the cautery at all of the fire, then the fire is so hot that it has this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand midway in that disease which is called "adubelati", until the cautery pierces the liver, and so that the cautery be cut like this that the patient feels pain from it in such a way that the flow of the pus is arrested.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cautery with fire by iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease which is also called "corrodens", and it's nothing other than a gangrene, because it corrupts the limbs as much as the fire corrupts the dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a person who can bear the fire cautery, then use the small and large cauterizations according to what is suitable for the patient or the disease; after cautering all parts until you remove all corruption, so that nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let him lie for three days, and put on small cauteries to suffer the burn with oil until the scalds of fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After this treatment for sprained limbs.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that a healthy limb does not form, it is good; and if this does not happen, restart the cauterization on the one that has remained corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this sickness has never been cured by medicine water in place of fire cautery; but fire cautery is always more effective aid, and I have already said the cure for medicine water in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of pearls that come to the bone.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often happens that a bone by accident gives birth to a sickness called "clos" according to our intention, and it's a great defect that causes the bone to break.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And there are two types of fire treatments for this sickness.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	Which is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is to heat the head of hair like a heated needle, and it should be made from good iron to penetrate the nail in all parts, with subtle edges; after that, put it on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until the blood reaches the font of the nail; then let it stand for three days until pus begins to form; then make an emplaster from fresh mallows crushed with vinegar, and apply the emplaster all over the night, and the nail will come out and be desensitized from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint of the elbow by applying a kind of poultice to warm it until it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by force of the body, and it often happens in hands and feet, it is fitting that you apply fire cautery with hot water; and it is done thus: take a cane made of iron or wood, or a feather quill, and put a clot on top of it and an alum; so as to burn warts; and place the cane so that it pricks everywhere, then put a little warm water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the margin of the cane comes to the root of the clot, and can find the hot water running all the way down to the root; and let the patient suffer a bit the burning with hot water for an hour; then leave it as is, and it will dry out all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Make a bandage after another until you have searched through all those who are in the body; then treat the limbs which have been constricted.
li cure dou trembler	Treat the patient with shaking.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some are trembling from cold, or from fever, a quarter, or from another cause, if it is fitting that you make four cauterizations above the spine on the back, one cauterization between each spine; one cauterization at the shoulder, and one over the stomach at the olive cauterization; let them calm down, and hasten to cure the disease of the cold fever.
des pustules puans	of yellowish pus.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never do they appear by chance in the body, or yellowish pus, that come from large corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary to perform cautery on each head of the boil: a subtle cautery of fuselage of myrtle, so that the point is grasped by fire, or from the root of aristolochia long, or with the cautery lens.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time do you cut when they first appear, according to this method, and it cannot grow in size or increase forward, but the superficial swelling that comes out is broken down, and it heals; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is struck.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often great bleeding occurs from the artery that is struck at the wound, or at the incision of the abscess, or with the cautery on a limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to be stinky.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Instruct the patient to apply a hot cautery to the wound as much as possible, so that the discharge does not occur again; then put olive oil cauterizations of various sizes, both small and large until they are all red; then, take one, great or small, according to the wound and let it see where the artery is routed; and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it catches fire when you lift your finger over the vein, and the cauterization has burned out, then take haste to get another from the cauterizations that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after another until it is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is near, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when the blood does not flow from the artery, one cannot stop it oneself when the artery is great, unless it happens by one of the four ways we have said: or through cautery, or through extraction when it has not been treated, or through strong binding with thread, or through medicines placed on which have power to stop the blood; and if it is tied and strained as a result.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will undertake the strengthening of a tightly wrapped bandage or placing things on it, or other similar things, if they are not profitable to do so.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has not a remedy or medicine at hand, he must place his two fingers over the vein wound as we have said, and strengthen it well until it stops bleeding from above the wound and above the vein; and do not move him, but let the cold of heat be applied often so that he becomes extremely cold until his veins are congealed and swollen and strengthened. And make incisions in the direction where it has need of cautery and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on treatments for stones.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	As we have said in the first chapter on all diseases by which it is convenient to use fire cautery or medicines, incisions and applications, and causes and symptoms and forms of the cauteries; and as I mentioned that book for the head just now, and I will go into this same chapter because one finds these things more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this chapter, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first cautery, and therefore you must take greater care.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to venture into folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who have been so afflicted with their disease that they easily die due to the force of their illness and the great severity of their malady; and because of this one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And to those who have given this their attention, and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the sick person is pitiless.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not for you unless you are agreed by those who come to you with this manner, but put more honor in your practice than in your desire, and do not act without careful consideration of what is in your power, and from that which you know, and from which you have experience; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your sick patients, so that their health may be converted; for this will help you to gain a good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three dear children, Our Lord gives you good understanding and integrity, and if it please you to aspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I instruct you to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
dou chief plein d’aigue	with a full head of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	We know that this disease often comes upon children at childbirth, and when the nurse ties too tightly the child's head; and there is no clear cause for it that we can see.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease without children, and in all those that I have seen, it ended in death; and for that reason, it seems to me that I should try these remedies in part.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw that in one child the joint was swollen with water, and the head became swollen every day until it could no longer endure; and he thought so much about the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled under the bone above the joint, between the cartilage and the bone; and the wound is such that if you cut into the cartilage below the joint, then you make a large incision in the head as long as two fingers, until the moisture flows out; and look at how the shape of the spatula
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the abscess is larger, then you will do two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the signs that you observe are on both sides of the jaw, and the fluid bursts forth when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not return: then it is necessary to do three incisions into the skull according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture entirely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After straining the incisions with cloths and powders, and putting in wine and oil, and leaving it for five days afterwards; then set free, and treat the wound by poultices and ointments, and leave to drain the skull, and then give dry meat a little bit of moisture until the limb is comforted and sane.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look at or open the large opening of the abscess, and gather up the assembled water; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right side, and sometimes on the left side.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure then the size of the abscess when you open it up and gather the water, and cut accordingly what you have the power to do; and be careful that you do not cover the artery; and observe how much blood comes out, so that the patient may die from the bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of the nose.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it has happened that a disease is called "cough" on the eyes or in the nose, and the disease is ancient, and the medicine cure does not profit at all, then the latest cure if is cutting with what you cover the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Instruct the patient to look backward when you cover their eyes; afterwards, rub them hard with a rough cloth until the arteries open up, then extract the patient's neck from under one cloth; afterwards, examine whether there is any vein bleeding out, and that the veins of both are after the ears, and they will not be returned soon; afterwards, sign the veins to close, then cut one and the other with a good spatula of II parts, until it reaches just to the bone, so that this is done over a large neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you look, pour out the spatula under the artery and cut it above, in the same way as it should be through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if you keep going down continuously to the top without stopping.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Et se li artere n'apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantite de l'espace de III doe, puis seigne d'enche et fent jus a l'os;
de emigrainne	They are going away
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old age comes and cough is good, because of moisture of tears and cold in temples and sores ancient and similar things, and it is treated with various kinds of medicine and no one profits from it, if we cut out the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have narrated.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way to extract them is that the patient makes his hair stand up on his temples, and listens for the artery opening in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is not fully restored like in some people who are too cold; and if it is restored, he tightens the neck of the sick person with certain cloths, then frowns on him with any harsh cloth, and warms up the lower part with hot water until the artery becomes manifest; then he takes a spatumile of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Instruct the patient to scorch the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it up towards the head with pincers, and carefully separate the threads that are under each part; if the artery is subtle, turn the needle to the point of the pin, then strike at that place according to the quantity of two needles.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if it is not struck, do not strike without causing pain in all its parts.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And pull the vein of six cuts, just as three; and if the artery is great, it is to be ligated with two levers of a double thread of strong silk, so that no purulence appears before the sound of the wound, and comes out in due time; then strike the superfluity which is between the two levers at that same hour, and then, if you see, since the cauterization with the cold cutlery up to the bone until the cuts are struck, it is the proper work, if the patient has no fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery, it is a remedy to finish the moistures: because of this it is more aid for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries, take out your left and fill him with clean wool and put on well-made tents; and when you draw them off, cure him with dry medicines that make charcoal, and with tents, until he is cured; and if not cut from the artery as much as you do work, then hasten to cover by fire cautery, or take out the vein of vitriol and strain it on your hand so that it does not become stained; and if you do not have this present, put wool on his vein as far as he will not be frozen, and let him cool in cold water until he is strained as much as it concerns; and what is more muddled and lighter to extract the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery with two parts, but the parts should be well-stuffed so that its heat lasts longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the instrument is too dark, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have two small knives one of which is a large mallet, and then when you apply salve to the two wounds, apply the hot iron so that it comes close to the bone, and cut the vein in two wounds; and be separated by two joints because there is no soldering with this cautery for all parts; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing into the veins that are on the forehead of the head, and it does not benefit from any medicine that is made, and you see the face of the sick person reden, and feel pain around the eyebrows as if from a blow; and the oil is thick and moist so that the hair of the face is wet, and the skin is scorched by the heat of the tears, it is necessary for this cure.
