Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called him the "cure contused", and you must tell the patient who has this illness to let his hair grow long on the head, then make three incisions or equally according to the length of the forehead; and one of them should be as if two doves were tearing at the front in a downward direction just like that; and the others should be two, on either side of the paper, and you must guard from the cutting of arteries which are there above the papers; and hold your hand back from continuing with the two mandibles, and each wound is as thick as three doves traversing it; and take a piece of sponge and some cloth to soak out the blood, then pour in the salve good of two parts.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is just above the temple, to the second incision; and scorch all the wound between the two incisions as far as the forehead bone, then make another part from the main incision just to the other second, and then extract this splinter.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you prick with the instrument called "cultellary" in the first cut, and it is sharp from one side and soft from the other, neither cutting nor scratching, this is the shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the cutting edge sharp towards the red flesh at the wound, and the soft edge towards the bone, and prick until it comes to the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut off today the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is complete just as far as that which opens the wound, and then make another cut in the middle until the other side; and then remove the blood equally, and express the fluid because of the blood taken; then put a linen cloth in each cut, and place soft drapes soaked in wine and oil and wool, and guard that swollen flesh does not come out; and on the third day remove the bandage, and administer great quantity of fresh water, with ointment basilicon with rose oil, and other treatments to cure wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Let your eyes rest
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any veins are congested and accustomed to that habit, and you see the eyes clouding up and darkening, and weakening sight, and papery things burning; and the hairs fall out, and pain is felt in the head, and the patient sneezes; then observe by these accidents that those matters and this congestion do not come forth except from many veins, and where it is, you should see it.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to turn their face, then make a great cut on both sides of the forehead.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the wound on the left temple to the right temple, and make an incision just as close to the bone; and keep your hand away from the temples that are moving downward; and when the bone is uncovered, suck out all the blood with a sponge, then sew between the two lips of the wound with cotton wool and linen; then tie soft drapes soaked in wine and oil, and be careful not to touch the abscess; when it is closed, you should rub the bone until it starts to discharge, then treat with remedies that promote drainage, which are known as "jargons".
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of flaxseed flour and 4 parts of ground poppy seeds, and mix them together; and administer them in these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All those things that fall into the ears are among the four kinds: grains, or fat, or stone from mines, or similar things like metal; or seeds, such as jujubes, fava beans, peas; or fluid-like things, such as water and ashes, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or some other kind of thing that does not fit in the ear and does not stick to the ear, if you put the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, put on some oil violet or olive oil, and then perform the extraction; and let it be turned out of the condyle, and stuff the nostrils with cloth or wool; and place a piece of cloth over the ear when it is turned out, and put the ear up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often the stone comes through this remedy; and if it does not come out, then you must perform the extraction with fine pincers, for thus is its form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it does not come out with the pincers, this is good; if not, you must extract it with an onion thread of fine double loop; and if it will not come out like that, make a chain of linen and pour water on the head through the ear hole very deeply, so that it cannot enter in through the chain; then take out the stone, for often comes out as we said; and if it does not come out in this manner, catch glue to pick up the stones, and put into some instrument with a point for that purpose, and put a little cotton inside; then press the glue on top of the stone or any other thing, and take out the stone.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot escape from all these things that we have said, then hasten to pierce the ear so that an abscess forms in it, and spasm; and the manner of piercing is such that you first make the patient's head healthy, and extract the blood according to its measure, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fat or where it depends, and cut it out as if it were a moon, until you reach the bone; then, with your skill, extract the bone quickly from your mouth; and the cure will be as long as he is made healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's pus that is accumulated and it swells, administer the extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then apply a poultice in this subtle form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that kind.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not cut it when you think the grain is moist because of moisture in the ear, unless you have made many cuts there first; then take out fine threads and from a vessel, as we have said, so that the extraction may be gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In water then what falls into the ear is fitting for patients to use an expectorant of condensed conditions, and fill the ear with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear or in water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it falls through because of this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If this does not work, he should pierce many holes according to the length of his nose must be tied and light, and let him warm it by fire; and put the patient an earplug or plug in his ear, and sail it on one side of his body, and fix another piece on the piece that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with bone and bone until the water dries out completely, and so falls the whole thing completely; and if you see it, pierce a joint, and pour one of the shavings into the ear, and the other side to heat, until the smallest joint is burned; then make another piece of joints as long as the water has dried out, just like we have said in the bone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of meat, if it is small in size, like a lump and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large in size so that one can feel it, extract it with pincers; and this is the lightest thing to remove which exists in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the removal of worms, put some ear drops in the ears, when you cure as we have said in the division and treating distillations; but if the cure does not work, then it is advisable to look at the ear in sunlight: if no worms are found, take a small needle to gently extract them; and if none are found, prick with a small pin because this is their form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And be narrow under and wide above.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in the ear; and this same thing happens to adults by stopping of the wound, or by cutting something inside the ear, and this stumping comes to occur sometimes from within the ear, if one cannot see it, and sometimes occurs without a hole, and the person sees well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That one which comes from within, if it cannot be seen, is due to inflammation in more dispositions, and in that case you must put the ear of the patient towards the sun; and look inside: if you see pus appearing, then the wound has this spotted form because there is this shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And if it is filled with pus and trenching before and behind all flat, if the ear does not bleed; but if the inflammation comes from a bone or part of the ear, if you have subtle fingers, and carefully cut until that charred thing is all bone.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	If the blood pricking occurs at the root of the ear, take a fine razor and shave it gently and heat it a little over the bone of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the blood pricking that the patient feels great pain in the ear, pick lightly, and keep from greasing the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the size of the perforation, and apply Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and apply rosewater ointment, and powder on vitriol brulet; if you see an ebb of the ear, sooth the place that you treat with another tent moistened in croton oil and beeswax, until the swelling is gone; then cure as long as he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if blood comes out from the wound, plunge an sponge in cold water and wrap it around the ear, and use other treatments that remove the decoration of blood which are for treating bleedings.
de la char des papieres	of the fat of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Bind the warts on the eyes when they are moist and dry, so that you stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and cut from a spatula of its roots; then apply vinegar to the affected part.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they do not fall off, if the cautery is applied to the lenticular part with fine fire, and after the incision, it brings forth wounds; and many times they recur, since nothing remains of their roots; and when those roots are cauterized by fire, they do not return.
de la gresle	From the horse
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	There come many times paper things that seem like gashes in their shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "grandine", which is an assembly of thick moisture on top and bottom; the symptoms are such: take care if grandine dries out from one side and the other, and it's a light thing to know; do then the donkey thus: cut it slightly wider, then scorch each part lightly, then pick it up with pinches, and strike.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it with a piercing just a little of the paper, so as not to grieve the patient; and if the crack is large, if the assembly has a seam, then continue the cure until it is healed; and if it's small, do nothing to force it, because the bandages restore it immediately and irritate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	There is a grease that is sewn onto the net of papers above, and this happens to children who are born without anyone, and their eyes weep much for them, and they come with cathartes in the mornings, and cannot see towards the light of the sun because their tears fall on their eyelids; and for that reason they sleep on their faces afterwards, and they put themselves asleep, and their papers above their eyebrows are wet due to the exinach grease which opens up in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the liver with your two hands and feel the exinach inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the sick person puts his head on your healthy one; then take a linen cloth, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach in each part, then put it on him; press with your hands from both sides so that the exinach is assembled inside the circle; then make a cut at the midpoint of the moisture towards the spatumile trenching a large incision, and not be greater than the wounds we made in the vein; and make the skin tight up to where you see the exinach; and from further circumstances comes exinach from the incision, according to the shape of white fatty meat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out the hair completely from one to two fingers at once, without any cloth, and turn your hand in both right and left so that it is even; and keep in mind that you should not add anything into the wound, lest you become affected by all the pus just until the oil has been applied, lest you burn yourself.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the cut does not open up immediately at the beginning of the wound, then apply a little to the wound lightly until it appears; then cut as we have said, then cover with cloth easily and coolly, and bind the leg.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break veins and put them up to corrupt that remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the patient should be safe.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to the left apendix hot, so the physician gives emplastrum salving as long as he is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs of paper are born, other than nature, and have grown old, and touch the eyes, they cause trouble and bring about kinds of illnesses such as excessive crying and softening of the papers and albumin, so that it is due to the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is done in four manners: or by cautery with fire, or by astringent medicine according to what is in front of the chapter on cautery, and it is made either by incision and suture or by cauterizing, according to what I will say.

It is necessary that you put the patient's head on your healthy one, then turn the paper of oil with your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, then prick an aglet into the thread above; and either take the edge of the paper or tie to the hair that grows above these hairs, and cut the paper at all with a razor; then make in the part below the paper, under the hairs, so much as from the great laceration to the small one, cutting according to the quantity you see extract the thread, and put underneath the paper a small tunic of cotton and drapery, then sew above the paper an image of encaustic, like that of myrtle oil, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the size you saw extracting the paper which is devised on all.

and if there is another way: and it is that you sew the paper with a figure which is as like the fuel of myrtle, just as we have told, at three times of six according to the form that is here
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take care of those who are already sick according to equal powers equally, following the shape that is here:

Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui. S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late and the cut has great force, then treat him until he is sane; and when the wound is sewn and if the skin is lifted, and the hairs do not fall again; and that is the form of the two ligatures you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	Instruct the patient to treat the wound if it does not come out with the hairs, so treat the wound under all that hair you have ordered, until the blood comes out from above and you see it through your sight; then treat the wound and the thread, close the eye for two days or three, till the hair grows in its place and falls off the head; and if small hairs are present, accompany one long hair with the chest nature, and lift them up with that one till they are stretched out and then lift.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil’s spoilage
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness is called "aleacratic" or the spoilage comes to the oil, there are two ways of it happening: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And happens suddenly by wound, or by incision, or by cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of it is that you cut open the wound, and serve the edges of it, and put inside linen tents, and tie them so long as they are clean; and it's not fitting to use only in the cure of things that dry up and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the sickness returns worse than it was before; but work on things that soften, such as fenugreek; and boil rose water or other spices, and seeds of linen, and apply a poultice made of melted diaquil oil, and wrap a tent around it, and treat with it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you give yourself protection so that it does not turn to a worse form than it was before; and this work that we have said is not made of fire only, but rather according to the shape in which the sickness first came.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat which comes to the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness, which exists below, is truly called "axacratic", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way of the work in such cases is that you take an awl, since it has two threads, and pierces into the fat, and makes punctures on both sides until the threads appear in two joints of the fat; then pull the fat over all with the awl, and pierce at one spot a foot long.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what it ought, that's good; but if not, take the razor and put it in the wound, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on both sides inside the paper; and let the joints of the two cuts meet at the two angles of the incision you made; and do it so that when they are assembled, the shape will be as the shape of a letter with the no «I griesche» ; then take away that fat, according to the amount that is below its skin, from what follows the paper, then join the two parts that are missing, and sew with a thread of linen; then apply the cure for what we said about medicines for softening, and stitches, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	Et if the sickness comes from cutting or stitching or cautery, so it is fitting that you cut an open wound beneath the hairs of the paper-thin skin; and according to what has been said before; then cut between the second and third fingers of a tent, as I have said; and one must make the work according to the form of the sickness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare an instrument of all sorts of power so that it can return the figure to its natural shape; and the sick themselves, according to what they need of work and instruments, and in more severe dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	for suddenly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suturing has happened to the hands in some way that the paper above is swollen with oil white and cannot move or do its natural work, so it is fitting that you put the point of a rasping tool under the paper, and lift it up; and make an incision as punctures, until you copy what is accurate at the subtle spatula, which should not be too harsh nor too rough, so that the patient can suffer neither the spatula too harsh nor the oil to bleach; and let your incision, from which you scrape away that assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it is healed all of that assembly, and does not happen again in the oily sauce salted with vinegar and sweet water, and milk; then put a linen tent between the paper and the oil, and put on the oil lard moistened with wheat; and after three days use the coliere and such rough things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the oil of the wolf
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	He knows that the wolf's joint is in two manners: it is nervous and looks like dried milk, and another which is not nervous but resembles congealed milky moisture; when touched with iron and cooked in its own pith, one cannot bear it anymore; and both resemble the great artery, growing little by little until they cover all the vein and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient places his head on a clean cloth, then opens his eyes; and raises a piece of paper with his hand, then tightens the joint as if it were tied in little double knots, and puts it above; then takes an awl, and puts horsehair, or goat hair, or bull hair, into its tip, very tightly; and punctures the joint all along the awl, ties the joint to a thread, and stretches it above; then scrapes off all the hair on the cost of the joint, from the point where the blood comes to the root, until they reach the skin near the head; then cuts off the remaining part in the root of the artery for about half an inch, leaving the natural color of the artery, so that by the incision no corruption or inflammation appears in the veins accustomed to it; and sometimes the joint is only incised with a single puncture, and at the tip, as we have said; then scrapes off all the flesh in the fullness of its subtlety, until it becomes soft, which is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And instruct the patient to let the scab not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the prunelike thing be perceived; and after the incision grease in oil a little bruised cloth, and put on a poultice around the neck, and leave it for another day; then cure as he wishes until he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not swollen and you cannot pierce it with the needle, and the nail cannot be inserted, this symptom of an ingrown nail is often cured with medicines; and it will sprout as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, apply oil to the patient, and take out the scab gently according to this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully remove the ingrown nail, and if you see that it is not shrinking at all, and the inflammation presses, then distill from your mouth onto oil mixed with poultice made of lye, and apply red poultice with bruised cloth, and let the oil sit for another day; then resume the other work according to the same operation, until it is entirely gone.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is against you in the oil, as in applying poultices, then apply the poultice to the affected area, and cure it first until it is healed, and then resume treatment as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the skin with pus does not heal in the oil due to great discomfort, if it is spongy and he applies a small part, without making more cuts, so that no blood comes out; then distill in the oil a scarlet collier, which is made from litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of flesh that grows on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	If some men do not get any red flesh, and cover the eyelid and restrain on papers and torn parts, as if it were a rose from balaustre; and the wounds are such that the patient puts his head in a clean place, then open the eyes, and coat all that flesh with nails suitable for this one, and support with strength; then cut the first flesh, and go cutting to the rasorer until to the end, and be careful not to hurt the oil at the treatment; and do as we said in the incision of the ulcer and small forces of which you should know what form comes after this chapter shows; and when the incision is completed and cut out all the flesh, then use the oil of sieil broiet or distill collier rouge and similar medicines corrosives, and put on the oil cotton with abin d'uef, so that it may be certain of the abscess; and if it remains nothing, and he does not get dressed, and you doubt an abscess, then let the oil and cure the abscess with soothing things an abscess; then return to your treatment until it is healed, and do thus coat the flesh in the oil by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	It is necessary that you alleviate the cure for each weak person on both natural and accidental roads in the presence of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these operations until you see if this member suffers from the aforementioned injury.
des voines des eulz	of eyes.
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are red veins that are covered on the skin, and they tolerate the pressure of the eye, weakening the skin every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, it is necessary to see first whether the skin is inflamed, and if it is, for there is no other disease that burns like the inflammation; therefore, take care in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on a healthy pillow, then suspend those veins until one hour according to his wisdom, and so place those subtle veins doubly according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two per degree in the four limbs according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then apply the force to those veins subtly, and suck out the blood afterwards another hour, until you see remove the blood forces from the oil; and beware that you do not strike the oil with the pointed ends of scalpels, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only extract those veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the oil rosewater and red to corrupt what is remaining in the wound.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to suck out all of it in that one hour, then apply a plaster on the oil with soothing things to relieve the pain of the eyes, and let it remain for some days until the pains are relieved and the abscess is secure, then resume according to this manner as before until they are healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	About the finger wound
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The arissati fistule: when you treat the wound with cautery and medicine, and it is not cured, there is an infection in it that must be cut open, at the abscess, where it must die, and remove all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see corruption and blackness, if it has all the equipment of which this is the form; and it is called "aspercief", make a needle from the iron on the head, and prick it as sharp as a file, in the same shape.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press hard enough with your hand until you feel that this corruption is cured; and do this no more than once, then restore it with medicinal extracts.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the head of the shoulder is soldered and charred, and if it does not heal, and the body of the arrow is soldered and remains so for forty days, and it does not renew and is no longer apothecated, and worse accidents do not happen, you know that he is sick; but if this is not so, then there is only another way to return the fistula to the puncture in the neck according to this form: and it is that you uncover from the bone the second time by iron, and with medicines sharp, and when it happens uncovered again as much as before, and take three iron pins and make the fistula smaller just at the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put the stump on the bone of the elbow, and remove your hand from the wound a little, then turn it all around until you feel the bone and the patient feels that he is coming when you hold his hand over the neck; and since you restore the stump with dry medicines as I have taught you, when the head heals and strengthens the leather, then apply the matter to the neck; for this is a lighter thing on the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are cut to the end in all directions and do not come loose from the eyeball, or even slightly, if you choose to cauterize the patient; then clean, then put on bandages or poultices with a needle to suck up the discharge, then put oil made of ice and aloe and incense and saccharocolle onto it, and then strain the oil, and apply poultices over bands and drapes; and do so in the manner that you take soft cloths, double each one four times, and then place one on top of another according to how many there are to serve; then strain from above with a firm bandage strip, and reapply poultices to suck blood until it stops bleeding; then remove the poultices and let the oil constrict for day and night, and if they become loose again, tie them up more tightly, if possible; then untie the binding after a day and a night, and if you see the discharge stop, that is good; but if not, reapply poultices and drapes and bandages and needle and suck blood until it stops bleeding.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	A fall from a rope or a ladder
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a rope falls on the head, then opens up, and comes out with pieces of paper like grains of resin, it is astonishing to see; so if you cover your eyes, the injuries are such that you stick an arrow into the root of the part below just under it above, then stick another arrow where there is double thread from the shoulder; and pierce them, and leave the first arrow according to its disposition; then cut the new double thread and tie a portion of the head tightly, then draw out the needle and apply olive oil in abundance on the wound; and let it be so long that the threads stick with the head, then treat the oil on comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is held by the rope every part around a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, then take the lancet in a subtle spoon that comes from within of oil, and remove the moisture albigne and descend the eyelids, and enter into them soon; then extract as long as they are sanitized.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the spoon of oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This sickness called "alcunnati" is not just the spoon of oil that is assembled in it, resembling water descending, but it's not water; and the way its appearance appears is such that you sit the patient on a stool, straight and upright, then take hold of their head with two hands, and watch how the spoon comes up to above your eyes; then let it be placed, do not remove, and see if they get better, or else light becomes dark for them, and see what is happening as usual; but if it doesn't come out below, know that it's water, and if the movements of the spoon are assembled like we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the patient between your hands, then take the thin spatula and apply it to the corneal conjunctiva with the continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and the crown, until the bowel is freed; and when she is out, distill in hot oil mixed with melted honey or fenugreek, or boiled wine and honey, then cure with another cure until she is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	As we have similar signs of the oil in the division, and what is needed to pierce it; if according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you place the patient between your hands crossed, and take a warm cloth from the light of the sun, and tightly bind the healthy oil; then put the paper of the oil on your left hand if your eyes are on the left, or on your right hand if they are on the right; then take in your right hand, if your eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or on your left hand, if your eyes are on the right; then place the point of the instrument near the crown by the thickness of a thread on that flaky layer of the oil to the lower side of the minor lobe, then courageously insert the "almagda" and twist your hand until you pierce into the flaky layer of the oil, and feel when almagda comes to the empty thing; it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the space between the pit and the end of the nail; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal tissue, and then put the instrument just above the oil, or on its side; then press it from one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the pain of the fever has passed now, so see the patient in front of him and the instrument on his table.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After the small rest, and if the fever rises again, put force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and does not rise, gently pull out the arrow in rotating your hand little by little; then put on a bit of cool juice and clean under that oil inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put on the oil a cloth or linen soaked in rose oil and a great quantity of ufe, and tie it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and for those of our time, put on a linen cloth with an abundance of ufe.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the arrow cannot enter in the oil because of its hardness, because there are some men who have too hard eyes, then it is convenient that you grab the instrument which is called "alberit", for this has a form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Et perceive donques la conjunctive soulement, 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	The head of the shoulder comes, which means you need to release the oil before the seventh day, and take care of the abscess that is causing it; and when it is appeased, then release the eye and put on its face a poultice for one day, and be laid in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then this patient comes, a little by little, and becomes accustomed to its case; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Land of Arabia, who told us that in some other country they used to do an operation with a lancet, by which they would draw out the water, but I never saw it or knew of it in our land, nor did I read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And this is what it looks like when they do not know the forms of alum, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are from pure arsenic:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head of this same subtlety is in three angled wounds.
de la char sor le neis	of charcoal on the skin.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There is no time when charcoal is not joined with other different things, because there are some that resemble scorpions to the point of being like pieces; and those with charcoal added in various colors, and those with soft charcoal like bone-colored charcoal.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore, in those soft chars that are not reinforced, it is necessary to place the patient between your hands against the sun; open their nostrils, and pour the vinegar on those chars, and apply hot coals; for as long as you can sustain it until spatumile (subtle knife), then take out whatever you can.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	In case the remains of anything cannot be covered, if you put all the instruments in order and lightly, they do not stay; and if they are not covered by any sort, or by an abscess, or by cauterizing, as is suitable, then cut as soon as possible, without delay. If it is a malignant abscess, hasten and cauterize so that they do not fall until the bone is dried out and all the flesh is torn apart, and either let or send to one who knows how to heal, hot water or vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the poultice is not applied and moistures come just in front of the palace, if it is considered healthy; and if moistures penetrate deeply as they should, consider that there is no bone exposed beneath, because the instruments do not come to cut. Therefore, it is fitting to put a fil of linen a little thick, soiled by hands, and with some powder on either side, and apply the patient's head into its poultice at some power, and smell it until it comes out from the poultice in front of the mouth; and this is a light thing for him who wants to do it; then hold the chief that comes from the poultice with one hand, and the other chief that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and check them one by one as we are sitting around the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Instruct the one who knows how to cut the hair so that he learns that nothing has corrupted that flesh, then take his son, clean the wound, and anoint him with Egyptian oil, and put it directly over the bone as before; do this three days or more, until the ointment corrupts all that remains of flesh; and then place a linen cloth on his head for some days until he is healed, and if he needs dried medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, because it distills oils and medicines into the linen.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or lead, shaped like a lampover, like a cloth, and conduct them in the same way; if you see this, make one closed and sewn, with instruments prepared for purging the head; and hold one hand on top of the head to hold it while you heat the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh on the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often it appears in the head of the neck a disease called "telul", and grows and becomes large boils, so visible to sight; and for that reason you must make a poultice at the beginning, and burn the bone all out, then apply hot cautery or medicine; and if one delays until they are big, if it is hard, of red color, of bitter taste: do not touch it with iron because it's an enchanted abscess, for when one cuts once, there comes great evil to the patient; and if the abscess is soft in touch, not of bitter taste, but you see how much can be covered, then make the patient empty himself and watch the poultice with fear, and treat him from dry things and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When they strike with a needle and skin
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	He sees that when the solution of continuity comes from one of these cartilaginous joints, he profits little, for it is not true in many men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to look at this carefully if the wound is fresh and full of blood; and then add the two lips to a suture, then treat the patient until he is healed; and if the lips are torn on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scar all the parts of their flesh until they heal, then reassemble the two lips to a suture, and tie it up, and powder with powdered antimony and incense broken, and apply it on top of the powder piece of emplastrum of strong or another plastering material, and let it sit on him for some time, then treat with ointment until he heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of sewing is that you assemble the suture: or with needles, as we have said in the suturing around the belly; or with thread, as I told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With your hands inside the lips there is an abscess, like grains of sand, and smaller and larger ones; therefore you must turn the lips, and split each one open, and take out with forceps and cut into each part; then apply vitriol to the incision until it stops bleeding; and then wash with vinegar, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the gum gets swollen because of an itch, which they call "albulus"; if you must, use tweezers and cut at its root, and let the blood flow out or draw it up; then apply vitriol to the incision, or other powders restraining and drying; and if that swelling returns after the second cutting and cauterizing, and many times does so, if you don't cauterize again, and this is how one treats oozes.
des sordens	of the ears
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	There is no instance assembled at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, with rough and painful scales; and sometimes there are black and yellowish teeth and pus, until corruption comes to the gum, and they become infected; if you must treat him so that he sits on your lap, and his hairs remain in your hand, and remove the teeth or the scales when they appear, not leaving anything behind; and do as I have shown for blackness and greenish color, and yellow and other blemishes, until they are cleaned up; and if it is found at the first attempt to take out a tooth, that's good; but if not, then reattempt the second day and the third day, until you have treated all of them; and know that teeth need various shapes of tools for removal according to what the work shows, because the ones who file on the teeth outside have other forms than those who file between the teeth; and these forms and others should be stored with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay the application as long as you can, because it should not be done like this; for it is a very high substance therefore we have no excuse to do the wrong thing.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to treat the tooth, it is necessary that you be certain about the shape of the tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the patient is that of a tooth, and suppose it is good, then treat the healthy tooth; and be careful not to depart from the pain by this means, as much as you can, until the evil causes leave, because we have never wanted to do this for these physicians; and when you are certain about the shape of the tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the inside of the tooth with a sharp instrument very hard to ward off the gum disease from all parts; then grind it down with your two teeth or with fine tongs until they are thoroughly cleaned, and then firmly grip the jaws; and put the teeth of the patient between your own cheeks, and hold them well so that they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth directly towards breaking, and if it does not leap forward, take any of these instruments and put them inside each part lightly, and move him as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are perceived and muddled, it is fitting that you fill them with cloths, in or on the places where they are broken; and if you tightly bind him with a subtle grip, so he does not break when binding; and it is very careful to put some oil over the gum for softening the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be cautious that you do not break it, and allow a part to remain, and reveal to the patient by the evil of the root even greater pains from the first.
