Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Be cautious that you do not do this as the ignorant master does, who by their haste and boldness break the cartilage every time, and do not bring to them anything but what we have told; but sometimes they come upon it by the vomiting of great disease through the roots that remain, or by breaking the cartilage, just as often happens; and when the tooth is worn down, wash the mouth with wine or apple cider and salt; and if bleeding comes, which often happens, apply a poultice of vitriol to break it; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the fistulas are when they have long pointed ends and large nodes, that they do not swell more when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And are large limbs if they do not swell when pulled out, and are iron made well, and are toothed to hold.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulled out, if it is advisable to put on the limb cotton moistened in butter once a day or twice.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the limb is softened, because with tongs that are called "algefry", the chisel seems like a beak of the knife; and they should be made just as sharp as a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not want to come out from all these ties, it is wise that you uncover the whole flesh around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which means the hook, for this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it is good and strong even if it does not break at all, and if the root bursts forth because of this, that is good; but if not, then you will have to help with all the instruments, for then the forms come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help it with this instrument that has two edges, for this is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front of the root of the teeth, and this instrument which resembles great pincers, for this is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Instruct the patient to hold the instruments with care so that they cannot break; and know that many of the bones are delicate; and also other instruments that should not be known; and the wise masters will test their own instrument according to what their work and the disease show, for there are certain diseases in which the ancient ones do not teach any instruments due to the diversity of these things and lest it breaks or injures another bone, so seek the instruments that you need, which I have told you, and help with gestures, because this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Let the instruments be large and well-fitting to hold the bone securely without harming it, but so that they can also remove it; and then restore him with the medicines suitable for this person, and if there is rot in the bone, even if it is small, so that he has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear to be different from their natural form and the shape is ugly, and also in young women, so you should know that if the teeth are not born after the tooth, it is not in its rightful place, and one cannot soothe or bind them: therefore cut the root; and if there is an eruption with the tooth, take this instrument of which we have the form, resembling the small beak, and it is of good iron, finely wrought in some.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth is cut with a small instrument every few days due to its hardness, and so that you do not disturb other teeth; if it seems possible to bind it, take one part of the binding material as is shown here.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also as the binding material that we make needles; and cutting with a small instrument gently every few days until the tooth comes loose; then smooth out the surface at the end with a file, so that if the teeth are too sharp they bite the tongue, you must bind the roughness so that it becomes even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth are loose, whether by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot bite firmly because they ache, then you should cure them with medicines that restrain, but these do not work; if they must be restrained with a thread of gold, for the threads of silver become green and rot, while gold does not move at all; so when choosing the thread, neither too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth; and if you observe that the teeth are coming loose, then take the thread and tie it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the stitches between the healthy teeth, as there are one or more, until you stop biting firmly at the sound of a healthy tooth on the other side; then resume covering where you started, and gently tighten your hand, so that it does not move at all; and be careful to tie close to the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Instruct the patient to take hold of the head of the shoulder with tongs, and assemble it, and put it between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not harm the tongue; and then let it be tightened as much as possible for as long as it can stay in place, and if it comes loose, or the thread breaks, strain it with another thread; if it remains and serves thus for its entire life, that is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of both healthy teeth and both molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, fresh as fresh, just like we have said; and do not let anyone intervene who is not learned and experienced, for at no time was the form of a tooth made from the bone of a cow, and the one that has fallen is put back in the place where it is defective, and strained as we have said, and remain and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Cover the tongue's joint
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is the joint that comes from below the tongue either natural or acquired at birth, but rather when some accident happens during a wound or from a bite. When treating such cases, work on the patient's mouth and head so that his teeth are in their proper place, and free the tongue; then cut open the nerve of the tongue, as far as the tongue is loosened from its bed, if it has any hard spot or injury, and apply a quick bandage. And make sure the wound is not too deep, lest the artery underneath is harmed; and when you have done this, take the patient to cool waters and a gentle treatment, or cold water, then place on the tongue a linen tie each night, so that the tongue may recover.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If there is bleeding from the head comes, apply vinegar to the wound; and if it does not come out, cauterize with cautery slowly, which is good for this one; then treat with another treatment until he is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see the pus in color, whether white or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if he leans towards inflammation, and there is moisture, take out the ulcer, and make a small spatumile, and deliver from one side and from the other; and if it does not come out to his wound, apply vinegar so that he may be stained, then return to his wound until you treat all of it; then lift him away with ease and with care, and cure with other treatments until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Wounds of the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	There is no occasion for the throat to have boils that are called "godath", and they are simply two amandrés, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, be careful: if it's a hard boil of small size and red color, don't touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also to prevent the bleeding; but let it be until it dies, and then you will remove it, or it would break on its own; and if they are white in color again, and the roots are subtle, you should have prepared an instrument to cover it, but first examine whether the boils are calm and have calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	So that the patient sits in front of the sun, and his head is straight, and he opens his mouth and the servant presses the tongue between his hands, so that this shape is formed; and it shall be made of either silver or fine gold, just like our scalpel:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue on all this instrument and you see the abscess, if you take an onion and a finger and put it into the honeycomb, and pull forth what you can; and pull none of these things out with threads, then cut at the instrument, so that there is this shape which resembles force; and see how the cheek is curved, and one side more than the other, and they are very fine, and it is made of iron or honey:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have that instrument, then cut with tongs, so that there is this shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Instruct the patient to hold still from one side and the other; and when you have touched one of the nuts, touch the other in the same manner, and after incision gargareze the patient with hot and cold water, and hot and cool, until bleeding occurs, if so gargarize the patient with a juice made from bitter pomegranates, or myrtle flowers, and similar things, until the wound is stopped; then continue the cure until the patient is healed; and when no more apertures occur in the throat beyond the two nuts, touch them like the two nuts are attached.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside the throat, namely the small sinuses; and I had tightly closed the entire throat so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she had stayed like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses are so swollen that they have been closed with two stitches through each of the two entrances to the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Therefore I applied a poultice at once and sewed it in one nostril, then rubbed with fire and took a great portion of the bowels; then sewed another in the other nostril and closed the mouth and pressed the tongue; after sewing an onion in these abscesses and cutting off a part, only a little blood issued; and now, I opened the conductive passages of the throat for her and she began to drink cool water and then wine, and did not cease cutting at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess reopened again, filling the hollow that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I inserted and cauterized within the throat: thus he remained still increasing; and I departed from these parts, and only God knows what he was after me.
de l’uve	from the wound
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the wound descends and it is pulled up and lengthened, if it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not large and round, if it is a "wound".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cut as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit from it, and you see that the swelling of the abscess is relieved, and it is subtle, so it is fitting to copy it; and the one that is round and assembled, but not long, this is a bloody or dark-colored wound, so you should close the incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner in which I have said about its shape and length, you should seat the patient in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we remembered here before; then thrust a needle into the wound, and pull it out slowly, and cut at the two places I mentioned earlier on the incision between the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you do not cover my force more than the excessivity which is outside of the natural term; for if you do it more, it will hurt your voice and tongue; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of cutting, it is necessary to use an engine at the cautery of the fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of cautery is water and dew.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts his head on your healthy one, and then presses the tongue against the instrument we have said in the cautery chapter, with vinegar hot cloth, not too thick nor too thin; and using the tip of this instrument, because there is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to place a single hair on top of their head with a spoon, and put the instrument over the hair so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine, until it does not come down to the throat or the tongue; then hold your hand firmly over the medicine and press on the forehead, for half an hour's worth of time, until you see the juice running out and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see, take cotton and put it under any instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and pour the instrument into the cotton channel above, until the cotton sticks to the forehead; do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and fall off after four days or five.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the cautery or incision; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamine and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and arnica and similar herbs, and assemble all or any of them in one pot, and add easily, and boil; and let the pot be well sealed with strong earth, and with the instrument according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And if of silver or tin, and if one of the nails is poured into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises up through the nose by the incision, until the nose becomes numbed; after this, it is repeated frequently, until the nose dries, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the advent of the abscess cold, for many things happen then, and do not make this more than when the abscess is receding.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If the fire cautery is not present, take a candle and put it inside his head an arrow of lead, so that the mouth of the patient does not have too much heat; for the arrow of lead does not let the vapor burden the mouth, and this is a good cure together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Sometimes this happens at the throat with a rope or an arrow of fish, or with nothing at all; therefore it is fitting that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun for the entire instrument so that you see if there is anything. What does not appear and returns to the throat, it is fitting that you make the patient vomit so that the meat may be cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing sticks after vomiting, or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of bread, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread; and tie to the sponge a thread, and then tie it again. When she comes to life, you will pull it out; and if she does not come to life from what we have said, take an instrument for diving in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Instruct the patient to let the hair on their head grow curved so that it can more easily enter into the throat, and have the head raised upwards; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest they come to life and do not push the bone inside; and make sure that the mallet is wet, for this will prevent it from being rough on the thing, so that when it is forced down, or it is treated with the instrument evenly, until it is completely through.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat cord
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Since it has no effect on the cord of the throat, as I have said in division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not benefit, then examine the neck of the patient towards the sun, so that you press the tongue to the instrument which I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, then if it has all that little one inch cuticle, or have thin nails that are worth those.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	But if it's not worth it, take a small thread of hair, and tie it around the neck of the sick person, then drink or swallow a whole hot iron.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is afflicted with cold water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full vessel of cold water, and cover the mouth, and let it be swallowed with senses moving, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the wound feels the water, spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not spit as we have said, then submerge the sick person in asafoetida, at the instrument that I mentioned for the fumigation of the wound; do this many times, because they will expel with tartar.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Instruct the patient to put a pot over their nose, where there are charcoals or charcoal vis, and cover it with a pierced cover in the middle, so that the keyholes of the instrument stick out; then administer the fumigation, and put the patient's head of the cage into their mouth, and close the mouth so that no smoke escapes, but comes straight up without delay; and now the vapors will take effect, and if they do not come out, repeat the fumigation multiple times; and let the patient suffer from thirst, eat unclean and salty things, and do not drink any water; and thus the disease is treated by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument through which one treats the abscess is thus: when one can see it, resembling curved tongs for nails to enter into the neck; and has the appearance of a spoon's beak, and has roughness like lime, so that what takes it cannot let go.
li chapistres des apostemes	The physicians who cut open abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many are like abscesses, according to what is remembered after each one in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways, one of which is similar to the other, because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for those who are within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	because the abscesses of the head are different from those on the trunk, and the abscesses in the thigh bone are different from those that come in joints, each having their own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if not to pierce those that do not need it until the bowel is dead according to its completion; and if of such there are who require piercing when they appear, and do not die as expected, just like abscesses in joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from the joints, and they are left until it is rotten inside, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is in the main limb and if you wait for perforation until it dries up, if it harms the main limb; or if it is near the foundation, if you pierce so that it dries up; and it is not wise to pierce an abscess when it seems like the digestion has completed, because fire will eat away from the foundation, and it will rot further inside, and a fistula will form; and cannot be healed in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is wise that you know the location of the perforation of the abscess which dries up according to the completion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the change in movement and the aggravation of the headache of the abscess, and other signs; and it is wise that you make the perforation sit so near or more dependent from the abscess, where it opens most; and let the perforation be long on the body, and if the abscesses are in hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and all like it, without any purulent discharge.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When these joints are swollen, according to which member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the groin, if it swells, let the perforation remain until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce in front of it, the blood will congeal and the body is filled with much filth; and by chance the lips and the fundament will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess you pierce according to the size of the body, according to which part the member has need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is fitting to pierce small abscesses in small wounds; and large abscesses in large wounds, and many cuts according to the similarity of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses as require that you cut the lock of hair, and cover; for when they have become as much as we have shown, and are softened, it is fitting to do so as one makes babies: and if there are those which are split into three angles, and those where one cuts like the juice of myrtle, like abscesses of blood; and if there are those where one does a round cut, and other sizes and shapes, and similar cutting.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, like an abscess that is soft and superficial, it is necessary to lance it straight; and when the abscess is large, and he has collected much pus, and you lance it, so that you don't take out all of the pus in that hour, but only take out one part; then stop the opening next day, then do not touch anything in that direction; do this many times until the bowel is completely emptied; similarly, if the patient is weak in virtue, or a woman carrying a child, or small children, or old men decrepit with age.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	But if you expect to see the issue of the bowel every time with the outcome of the lance, and by chance, the patient dies, do not despair.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then shrink from this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if it issues a wound, and examine whether the wounds of the abscess are small; and if it is an open lancing, then apply linen or old cotton cloths; and if there are large abscesses, and much pus, it is advisable to insert tenths in each one so that they come into contact with each other; and if you have struck at the abscess a part of the hide, and you have turned inside, it is necessary to fill it with old cloth or rasp of fine linen soaked in moisture, and tie it on the third day; then apply plaster and ointment until he is safe.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood has escaped to the right side, apply cool and gentle water, and wet the cloth, and tie it around the place that will heal many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood does not persevere, apply gentle treatment and cure, and the powders that I have in my hands in this book, and if it is winter time, and the place where it was injured is very nervous, you should tie on tourniquets and wet cloths soaked in wine and oil hot; and if it is still, and the place is charred, you should cover it with wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and oil hot, every third day, as we have said; and then remove the wound, clean it up, and cure it, as it seems proper, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what one must know universally in treating abscesses: or you have said how to go before the treatment of abscesses, and here it is told by the physician.
des soros	of sorrows
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head wounds come to produce small abscesses, and are like those in cloth, just as the hair of a goat, and there is much similarity.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also fats and such that are moist like pus; and there are those of flesh which are due to moisture just as worms, and there are others that are hard and stone-like in cutting, and there is no doubt about them if the arteries do not cause opposition.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the wounds of the belly so that you will know all instruments which are called "entromissoire", because the form comes after, what kind it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	If it contains moisture, they do it over long hair.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is empty, they scratch without leaving anything on the skin that contains that moisture, because it comes back again when they leave nothing; then plunge cotton in ointment Egyptian, if present; if not, in water and wool, and apply to the wound, and let it remain until the next day; and those who are left for a night will come.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then reapply the cotton as before, on the second day, and the dressing, until you know it will not stay for a night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable to him, until he is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscesses hold no more fat, he will cut according to this form, on long hair; and you will pick off the sinews, and scratch from all parts, and put all your care of traction behind the cloth where it lies; and if the arteries make against you, do what I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do also of the abscess if it is hard, and with cutting and with curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the size of the hard abscess is taken and the moisture, if it is lighter, for there are few bloodlets.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if it is so that any of these abscesses or swellings do not have moisture, and I showed you examples of such abscesses as were taken from the head of an old woman; and I found this abscess to be like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if anyone had burned with it, one would have done just as well a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come or swellings, whether they come on the head of children and on the roots of the ears, open them if they are all day to the lowest part, in order for the bowels to come out; and treat as it is necessary.
des scrophules	Wounds of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often they form abscesses in the neck, and under the armpits, and sometimes under the skin, and one swells with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly located in its own spot, as with the abscess and swelling of the head, as we have said; and the symptoms of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some swellings that contain moisture, and there are others that are malignant and do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In the one that you see has good flesh around the armpit, and is like the color of the body, and is silent in all parts and is not inflamed near the neck or artery or vein nor deep; so it is fitting to cover it up, and scratch off each part, and let the two lips swell with redness as one would have done on an abscess of the head; and take it off a little by little, and be sure that you do not uncover the nerve or vein, and do not make scratches or cuts too deep, lest your hands fail, and you see too much beforehand, so that you do not cover more than what is necessary.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	Instruct the patient to apply vinegar or an artery if it cannot be closed, so put vitriol in the wound, or any powder that stops blood, and hold the wound tight; and leave it until the abscess is eased and the pain is reduced, and then start to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the swelling is not drained, return to your work until you complete it; then ask your assistant if there are any small scrofulae remaining, cut them and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, do not cut that scrofula at its root, but rather tie it with a double strong thread, and let it fall loose without any trouble; then apply to the wound linen soaked in Egyptian oil.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you cut the scrofula entirely, it is fitting that you assemble the two lips of the wound and sew them up now, because there will be no more swelling due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is fitting that you understand to cover the root of the thing, and treat with force, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have swelling, pierce it or cut through; and treat as we said before, depending on the situation, then apply poultices with ointment and similar things, so that the corruption does not spread from what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, apply ointment to staunch its flow, until it becomes healthy.
de squinance	of squamation.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old people said and spoke about the cauterization of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land do it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	It is necessary for those who have strangulated that the rupture of the throat, which is called "epiglottis", be avoided; and do not attempt to help them because all the veins and the membranes in the mouth or in the throat or in both are inflamed due to the severe cut in the mouth or in the throat.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the channel of the membrane, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis so as not to escape the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four one small incision across, between the two circles or according to the size of the incision across the cartilage; and if we do so, it is very advisable to cut the epiglottis in such a way that there will be no cartilage left, and the vessel is long in reaching.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	Instruct the masters to extend the skin of the neck to the entire length when they are fearful, then split the wound so that it comes to the chenile; and exclude the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then strike the soft part, as we have said; and this will be proven by the section of the falix of the chenile that has sprung forth from the broken limb, and by the failure of the voice; and let the wound close over a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed by which you doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the blood vessel, and remove all the membrane so that the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce ulcers, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Because of the danger that one will not make this just when the throat is completely stopped, and the patients are judged to be at death's door, and the defect becomes clear.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	The cautery of fire instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a maiden took out her knife and pierced her throat, and cut off some of her breasts; and I was summoned to cure her, and found her dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found out that it was from the blood that had come out of it; and I realized she hadn’t cut herself by vein or by cutting through a nerve, but came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I rushed and stitched the wound, and cured her until she was well; and it happened to the maiden that she had only become red of voice, and returned after being put back in shape; for this is why I say there should be no fear with cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This is a hernia of the throat called 'hernie de gorge', which is a large swelling in the color of a jay's feathers, and it occurs mostly in women. It is two kinds: natural and accidental; or if it is not due to any engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is in two ways: for one it resembles a fatty lump, and the other resembles an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be treated with fire alone, but in those who are small, and test and search all around the vicinity. If you find it just like fat, and do not sense any vein, strike as we strike flesh, and take out its head, if it has none; and carefully search thoroughly, and treat it as needed, until it is completely healthy.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways to treat us, of which I will speak all the similarities; and it is necessary that I tell all the differences between good and evil.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is then fever and inflammation until the heat has passed, and it has been completed with putrefaction; therefore rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the evil there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the abscess, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the flesh, and begins just as a lump, and grows accordingly as a mass; and are like these similarities, or grime, or moisture, and are much of color like what I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure with no one, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form whether it belongs to a chapter or what follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you apply or moisten more than what you find in the abscess, and turn your thumbs little by little, until you see that the instrument has pierced the vein, then, according to the size of the abscess.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture comes out through the cut, whatever color it has, as I have said for other abscesses; and if the instrument does not come out moist afterwards, you know it is fat, so make a cross mark on it, then take hold of it with pincers, and lightly scrape it from each part, and beware the coat where it lies, in order to treat it sound with your nose; and if you cannot treat it sound, then cut it into pieces so that it does not stay there.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it stays in that place, it will come again many times; and if it stays for a little while and doesn't cause any grief, apply the wound with some corrosive powder sharp, and hold tight the wound, and put on soothing things near the abscess, and cure other wounds until it is healed; and if the pain is great, cut off two fingers from the wound, and cure the one who caused the injury to die.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein bursts against you or something else when you rush to it and apply the vinegar of vitriol, cut off two days or three, until the wound has dried, and rest from the bleeding; then return to cover that which it has caused to stay outside.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Now here are the forms of the interstitial discharges, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and among them there are three quarters called "albaret," and one called "breb"; and they come in three forms: great, medium, and small, to enclose the abscesses of fistulas; and are also like the needles with which you sew the sores, made of citrine thread, iron, or silver; and are yellow, but prove useless for enclosing the black pus of fistulas; and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small, according to the size of the fissure.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the cancerous tumors are many in appearance, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and there are tumors with two heads in three manners; and those with three heads, and likewise in three manners; and there are tumors with two heads and only one head, and likewise in three manners; all these are necessary in their own place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these are cut in such a way that they are sharp, and some of them are not cut from both sides, which burns the flesh, because of this one does not cut the vein or the nerve; and those who penetrate are replied with hammers, so that the patient does not lose anything at the opening of the abscesses; and there are three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see; and none should be used more than in the chariot wood, such as legs, arms, and nipples, and joints, and similar uses; and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling scratches on fistulas, according to this shape, with which one stains the blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And put it back at no time on a limb that is healthy with veins cut open, and arteries, at no time will they return to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never do the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they resemble the breasts of a woman; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wishes to cure them, should follow this form according to these lines from page .b to page .g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scorch the fat, and apply a plaster of medicine mixed with charcoal, then assemble the two lips of the wound to the skin, and treat it until it is healed; and if the nipple swells downwards and is deformed as in women, so that one becomes stuck to the other at the end of both, if they do not separate, because the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from page .b to page .g; then scorch the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suturing and powders, and what is necessary for treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or if the incision is not complete, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the decrease in blood, so that you fill the wound with wet cotton cloth in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it absorbs the remaining fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	The evacuation of blood when incising an abscess, and incision on a bone, and curing wounds, and extracting arrowheads, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	The abscesses that come from below the joints are hard swellings or where it has ribs, and if they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture therefore must be cut according to this form, from the line .b. (at) the line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire bow that is in the abscess is empty, apply the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment suitable for those until they are cured.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like swellings similar to scrophules, then cut it in the same way as we have said for cutting scrophules, and if the wound is in a place where blood can be let out, apply fire cautery as we have previously stated.
de la routure de l’artere	When cauterizing with fire
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin is burned on top of it, if it often leads to abscesses, and similarly also happens with a vein that has fled and an abscess; and if one examines as such when it's for the artery, then the abscesses are long in that part by length; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel strangulation; and when it's for the vein, there is often a swollen appearance; and this is folly to cover up this abscess, and even more so when it's below the joints and angles and around the neck and in many other places, and it causes great swelling.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to shun the cure of iron, and one who has a head should also shun it; and in those with an inflated artery, do it above the skin so long. Then sew around the neck as tightly as possible, and carefully cut open the artery through the skin; then insert an arrow into the vein on the other side, and tie the artery with two strings of twine for 12 fingers; when you see no blood coming out, and the swelling has disappeared, point to the source of the abscess; then apply the cure that is drawn from the bow, until the ties begin to form; and treat this wound according to what is necessary, until it is healed; and if the abscess was due to the size of the vein, you should tie off that part of the skin with your hand where you can remove the abscess entirely, then insert an arrow through the tied-off part, so that it runs from one side to the other; then tie off the abscess as I have told you, or tie a string of two parts around two fingers of the knee; and if you doubt whether the strings will not come loose, you should reinsert another arrow on both sides of the entire abscess through all the cuts made at the first insertion, and bind the strings in 4 fingers; then cut the abscess until it is dry, and then cut off the dried part, then apply a soft cloth soaked in wine and oil, and then bind up with bandages, and treat wounds of tenters and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	There are abscesses at the nails.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses come to the artery and vein, when the nails are exposed, or because of excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often at the joints and in the toes, where there are bones, and it's a grievous abscess, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and is more prone to cause pain; and when they try to restrain it with force, he feels great pain, but not because of infection of the body, but because of poor hygiene; and it's very painful all over, and doesn't move forward or backward, neither above nor below, and those who have joint issues should not be covered in iron, for by chance they might contract an abscess; and those who are on the head or forehead, make a poultice with the spatumile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have one pair of shears and cut it at its root; and if it is large, if the wound breathes, then scorch it, then scrape off the dead tissue, put the bone back in place, and sew up the wound as best as you can until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of great sores hanging around.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There is no case of this disease in the belly or any other part of the body, and it is called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots and large bones; and there are small and great ones; and I saw a man who had two bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, and they did not have any difference, they were white, and they had thin roots, and they were cut open, and decayed due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	Inscribe these and you will find in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI ounces, and the works done through the incision are such that if you look carefully to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist with a subtle root; if it is touched with the spatula large, and be present with the cautery fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting comes many times great hemorrhages of blood, and if you do not wait, then haste with the cauterizer; and if you see the patient is fearful and fearful of the incision on metal, take a thread of plumb well made, and tie the artery as we have said, and let it remain for two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to strain the thread of plumb until it cuts the artery, and feel by him the work done; and if the roots are large, then fear with cutting myself in the same manner on the belly, but you can cover half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be careful that you do not cut the joint which is of fiery color and poor sense and of clear sight.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	This is an enchanted abscess, and I came to the cure of this boil after.
quant li boude ist fuer	When a bubo occurs
