Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is therefore fitting, then suitable fumigations are to be used for this: none of the ancients have tried the fumigation with creosote and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument by which you are to fumigate the woman, when holding back the flowers and the second toe if it is that:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be seen similar to a cauldron, and put the subtle head in nature, and the hairs long on the fire; and so the fumigation upon the coals, and the itch until it is consumed, and another takes its place.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	For every child is born who has not pierced the foundation, unless one subtle syphilitic is suckled: if it is therefore fitting, then let them pierce that syphilitic in its fundament, and not with a spoon, so that the garment does not touch; then put on a moist linen in wine and oil, and apply treatment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, so tie a rope around the body flat, and let hands rest for days, and be put away when the child gets up to walk in rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes comes a sudden stopping of bleeding from a wound or an abscess; if it is covered quickly, if it heals, just as we have said about tying the body flat.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodules, and those that come from under the foundation before or in the space between the two parts, if there is a fistula or more; and when an old nodulation exists, it causes work, and makes moist skin turn white or subtle bowels, and sometimes these fistulas pass through; and they are caused by egestion or flatulence when the patient makes egestion, and by chance one passes through some way.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that occur just above the bladder, and just above half of the penis; and they reach just to the joint of the thigh, and no further from the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so you will know where the fistula is running to its end, and not to its start: and it is that you put your finger into the bottom of the fistula, and insert a sharp needle made of iron or thread into the fistula until it has some curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, then you put a thin membrane of parchment or the hair of a horse into it, until you feel the membrane or the hair at your mouth; and if you do not feel it, and there is no passage of blood, no swelling, nor odor, as we have said: seek whether it does not pierce through; for so you must hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is passed beyond the bladder or just beyond the urethra, so that it comes out and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is noticed at the joint of the crotch, then the attempt comes to be done on the left; if there is no curvature and the invention of pain around, then it is that they get stuck in the bowels, and none of these remedies are effective except labor, and vain attempts by foolish doctors who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those that are not perforated and are not old, there is hope for health by iron, as I have found, so that the patient lies on your hands above his back; and lifts up his legs until they reach his crotch, and bends his knees towards his stomach; then pours a poultice of hay or plonk into it, if it has curvature, until you see where the poultice comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the joint, then it is advisable to put your thumb index into it, if you sense any movement while applying pressure; and if it is discovered that there is a sequestrum or a chip in your bone, then know that she is painful; but do not work on it unless we cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	But it is not always possible to heal everyone, but this occurs rarely; and the aid that we give, if it is done carefully, as has been said; and put a hot braid into the fistula, until it comes from the bone root; and do this twice or three times, until you know which of these chips must be burned off, which resemble a bird's feather; and then apply the cure of soft bandages wrapped in butter, until those chips are gone, then the cure of splinting and nailing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, this is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is so, he cannot be healthy in any other way. And if he presses between them, and does not cut exactly at the foundation, and between his tendon and the tenting a thick covering of char or silk, and you see the fistula beneath the thick layer red with heat; if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and pour it away before the tenting, and apply cautery afterwards, as long as the head of the tent comes out, he will be freed from the tent and cured; then he should be given those charred things that resemble an owl's feather, and not remain sick.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he does not swell up and cuts between you and the work, so that the cautery by fire or medicine is applied.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Car the fire cautery has two things: it is to know that it is the swelling of these charred bones joined together, and the incision of blood and the drying of moisture; then treat the moist tendons in butter or in cold cheese, until they lie flat, and make sure the bones are dry in the wound; then cure the wound of sudden ointments in joints of dry flesh, and those medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When it is restored, if it is safe and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes just to the bottom of the wound and is separated from the body, then put two or more pounds into it and inquire about them.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tendons, and there are two of them or charcoal, or it is close to piercing, if all that has been done is sight by chance and hope, by the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you cut just to the bottom, or if you can, put tentes and cure as I told you; do not go too deep, lest you cover the foundation that holds the wound in place, and come out with the excrescences by chance; then cure, as we have said; by chance, it may be healed, or you will remove that covering which has been over the wound after it has been pierced at its bottom, or by tentes or another instrument appointed; then examine the false char that is in the wound, until you can; then study to restore the wound and keep the fistula away from the part opposite the foundation: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way; and when you put a tent over the fistula, and it sticks to the bottom of the skin above, then take a tent that is perceived at the head according to this shape:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put the twisted thread into II, and put the tent all over the twisted thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the bottom within, then extract the thread from that puncture, as far as you put your hand on the foundation; and take out the head with the thread, and assemble the two joints together, and hold one to the other, and let them be for one or two days; and restrain it at any time, until the threads are worn down these characters that are between two, and closed. Then cure the wound until it is sound and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not heal or is cut open, pierce it in all ways that you can, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not advisable to tie up the wound if it is too deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it heals.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spasm of the spine, from which a fistula is made, is much acute in one part and tense, and on the other not at all, for this reason one should not pierce what one should not pierce, as you see:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there may be small or large ones, and sometimes they have a clot attached to them, and there is one or more; but those that are outside the fundament do not have much moisture, and are covered in a thin membrane or some pus, and their color is similar to that of the skin. The cure for these who are inside the fundament is such that you instruct the patient to expectorate in bed until the fundaments stop bleeding, and then the thread becomes visible; if it does not come out, tie the malaide tightly with a tight bandage or cloth, or a piece of chamelot, and pull them off with your two hands, then cut, and powder over with hot powdered ingredients that are suitable for cautery, as said in the chapter on cautery, because the cure of other cures until it heals; if the fundaments cannot come out, tie up tightly, the malaide with a hard tie, to make them bleed, so that it can be seen whether they will come out fully.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is fitting to tie the bandage according to this manner: take one finger thick and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread up above and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two joints around the thread below the needle, if they are tight; and then bind the thread firmly, but not too tightly, and pull out the needle, and do so for all of them, and leave one to hold back the flow of blood; then put a soft fabric on top of the wound in oil or rosewater or ceruse, and put it on top, and command the patient to rest; and then let him sleep until he wakes up, and when he is well again, if there are treatments for pain and other treatments, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	And with a sharpness of thread or fabric around the wound.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It happens often severely with fever in the intestine, and due to the constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to reset at the point of a splinter or at the angle of an ulcer, which does not leave it moist; then treat until it becomes sound as if it should; and if it cannot become sound, repeat the rasping stronger than before, until it heals, and is scorched; then treat until it is sound.
dou fremit	do not be afraid
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	The bee sting is a small, unneeded appearance in the body, and goes deep into it; and at no time does heat form, and one feels death-like sensation from the tremble, and comes to all the body, and more so to the hands than to other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Instruct the patient to take a thorn from an owl's feather or a hawk's strong feather, and place it on the inflamed spot, until the mark of purple appears all over; then turn your hand around the thorn so that you cover the entire mark, and press the thorn into its root, and make sure its roots are secure.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this of a thorn from iron or stone according to this form, and be subtle below and careful above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, lest you damage the two, and press them. And if you see, cauterize the mark, as it is before or in front of the fire cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a cyst.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is one made to drink from an iron cup or an arrowhead, or melted tin or cauldron; and never are these small and great instruments used, according to what they are meant for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore these instruments are used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, which are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cup is small and great if it is used too tightly or if the belly is bound according to this method:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if there is a defect or the belly is bound, as you see, and the cup is inside perceived; and has one side pierced on each side; and is inserted into one of the sides, and into the other; and put into his belly with medicines in a vessel of best or parchment, and perceived all around by small holes, and between each hole there should be one space, then fill with hot thread, tight and strong as a nail, through X or whichever spot inside, and assemble the belly like a pig; and when the medicine is inside, if it sticks to the instrument in front of a thick thread, then cauterize; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And so the medicine should neither be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with oil or bear grease or similar thing, then pour it in lightly; then grasp the minister's hands together as much as possible until he is fully awake, then pull out the splint, and lift up the sick man's legs to show, and if the medicine comes out as soon as it can; and if he sleeps a whole night, so it will be more aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you splint him in a sickness of descending stomach, and the medicine comes out quickly, he will reappear as soon as he is fully recovered.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there are hemorrhoids on the fundament or abscess, so that the splint is as subtle as for an infant; and this is the form of the subtle splint where the skin is stretched.
des plaies	Wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	Since we have spoken in the division of wounds about the cure for wounds; or you will say the treatments for hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the place or places where the wounds are made, and why they were made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Things by which wounds are made are caused by falling on stone, and the cutting of a sword and knife, or lance or staff or seat, or similar things; or because they were made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that chokes on the neck, or on the head, or the shoulder, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you about each type of wound, and begin with simple wounds on the head, because the remembrance comes in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I dis that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it's due to stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is great, and you doubt lightly of an abscess: then do so immediately to heal the cephalic part itself if it came from blood of the wound, and be healed on the opposite side of the navel; and avoid the patient being replete with wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not heal, if it is weakened by food, and does not drink wine, nor eat flesh: and put on the wound, if an abscess comes out, apply cotton soaked in olive oil only, or rosewater; and if there is no hot abscess, if it is fresh with all its blood, and is moved only by air, powder, then I will tell you a little later; and if he has moved it, apply some ointments until he heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is very large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by stitches, then they must be assembled by suturing, just as I will say for wounds in the abdomen, of the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered bone and flesh, and it will not hold but for a little bit if you press; then treat the wound with medicine, and cover hard skin in its place with leather, and instruct the patient to eat thick foods, just as eggs and cooked bread, like fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or leather that is putrid, and it does not stick to the bone, if you press out all the putrescence, and drain off the blood, then treat the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound without a covering, which cannot be stopped with medicine, you must cut through it, and if you find the artery loose, tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	If these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you put on this powder which binds just as much as the art has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is thus: take an equal part of incense; one part of dragon's blood; three parts of vitriol, and mix it finely, apply the wound, and bind it firmly, until it has dried well and joined all its blood; then tie it well, and let it stay loose if it does not swell, for you do not stop the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes only vitriol is used alone, when you don't have the incense or the blood of the dragon, but the art has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the arrow has moved the wound, while it is still in that place, do not put any of this powder on it; but put some ointments prepared or made from chickpeas flour soaked in water and honey until they have set; then the cure should attend to other treatments until he is safe.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, if you carefully pinch the edges; and I will tell you later after this about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck-wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, if there are no differences between this and a fracture of the head; but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	For the shoulders if there is no other solution than to leave the cure and not put anything to restrain it, because the night brings it back and makes it retreat; and do not put on the wound anything that harms, for the substance of the blood is cold, and the continuation of the fever is with the brain, which is in the higher members; but if it's a medicine so, as calomel laved in sweet water, and melted with olive oil, and cured again in sweet water, and other stones from mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, so cut and bind with bandages, then the cure until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and he has a head full of blood, so cut below it; and if an artery is cut, and blood comes in, then seek to remove it, and apply ointment, and cauterize as necessary; and if the spine on his neck is cut, or the throat, and the cord must be guarded, because the flesh goes, so sew the wound above the vein of the neck, and touch only the vein but not the neck itself according to its natural shape; and then bind him at once, and let him rest for a few days, then his cure with ointments dried out until he is healthy; and if the wound has made a depression in the bone, so seek it; and if there are pieces of bone, so burn them all up you can, and what remains do not have, leave as long as the wound gets worse, and is freed and alleviated the discharge; and if the wound is fresh, so powder on top of the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has an abscess, then the treatment is as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a lance or sword wound.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a stab from a lance or sword and the wound is deep, then look carefully at the wound to see if any movement occurs: for this tells you that the wound is mortal; but if it's not deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it, nor bind it tightly for the wound until it comes out completely from bottom to top, and turn back to heart, and comfort the patient. However, apply soothing ointment, and tie it twice a day; if you don't have ointment, put fine cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if no spasms come, nor severe pain of heart, nor any straining movements from death occur; and when you see the bones taking their normal disposition, then you will know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds of ten and other treatments, until he is cured; and if she cannot be cured, and does not operate, then seek that there is an abscess; so you should do.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it's simple, deep, or on the back, if the treatment of what is in front is applied; if it's large, suture; and if it's small, powder; and if it has been pierced into the bone, and broken pieces have entered, then as needed, remove the splinters if they are exposed; and if not, leave the wound to dry out, because it will relieve the extraction of other wounds; and for other wounds, follow the judgment of other limbs as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	a fall into the stomach
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I will translate the text line by line into English.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	When it is cold, heat him thus: moisten a sponge or half a drapery in water, or heat wine squant and cypress and spike, and remove the inflamed intestine until the swelling subsides; and sometimes do this while the wine restrains, and he becomes muddied to be able to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine with water or boil and mash them, because by this means is alleviated the entry of little things; and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound on the instrument by which they are struck, as for the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is that he swells until he shrinks, so that none should cut him unless there be great need and there is not. And this is the means to break them: tear into within the container and do not stop it, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	When the wound is enlarged, and the intestines burst forth, so that it returns to its natural place in its own proper form, if you have the power, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, it is to be preferred that you put the patient on his back, and lift up his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, it is to put the head and the navel higher than the lower parts, and in this way as soon as possible apply the rule for great and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, do what is fitted out for you; then take between your fingers a soft minister who takes all the gore with his hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common method of stitches, where you prick an needle or more, according to the size of the wound's largeness, then leave space from the head of the wound two inches, and prick a needle with strong thread; and pierce both sides of the skin with both sides of the needle, which is under the skin, as long as you make it pierced from that side; and assemble both sides of the needle together four times; then tie the thread around the middle of the needle, two parts, and assemble the two sides of the wound together now, and leave space again, and prick another needle; then do so with the same needle, and do not cease until the whole wound is sewn; and it's best to have medium-sized needles, neither too thin nor too thick, because thin ones cut through all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot fit well into the skin: for this reason they should be medium. And it's not good to push the needles too far out of the skin and towards the flesh, so that they do not prick and open the wound before the stitching; then pierce the sides of the needle, which do not annoy the patient at night, and tie or drapes to the sides of the needle to hold fast, and leave them until the wound is sewn; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because there's a needle with two stitches, and it's common, that you assemble both sides of the skin and the two sides of the gauze together around a needle with strong medium thread; and when you have pierced all four sides, tie the needle to the side where you started, in the way one counts the threads; and put space between each stitch the thickness of an inch. This costure is for men who are seven years old, and I stitched a wound on a man who had a cut on his belly, which was infected by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and it was filled with intestines two palms wide, and it was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	The patient had the intestine removed when he was 22 years old, and the wound was closed after 15 days, and treatment, and was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they thought that he was dying, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where no one is found, nor any medicine; but put more cloth above the wound for two times a day, and washed it with water of honey until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you two proper ways of suture: take the needle and draw the thread from the side that is before, up to the same distance as the wound; when it penetrates the vein or artery in straight line, then take out the needle on the other side of the body, so that you pierce both sides, just like a peltier makes nails for leather, leaving once the suture thread from one part and covering it with the other, until the entire suturing is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of sewing is what the Galens call properly, it is like that which anyone makes, who puts together the two parts in a natural way, and calls one from one head to another, in this manner: prick an awl or near the chief of the mirach and pierce only that one, and leave the two joints together; then turn the awl and pierce from the back towards it inside the joint; then pierce one and the other from the back towards it inside the other side, on two more joints of the mirach on each side; and this is the manner of sewing in which there are many.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Galens say this word, and no one else testifies to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles if there is thread in each; and you must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other side, like those who sew corsets; and know that when the rupture is inside the belly, the sewing is more grievous than of the others on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The jugements of the wound are such as those of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, in so much as if the arrow has moved it, then reset the intestines and the cut; then apply powder with saltpeter and charcoal, and if the arrow has moved it, put on any ointment present, until the wound heals; and clean the fillet, and solder the suture, and the mirror; then cure the wound as other wounds are cured, till he is sane; and if you do not have medicines, then apply, immediately when they come to heal, cotton wool, and move it two times a day, till it be sane.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	But you do not need any other medicine besides for the simple wounds; and if you are in doubt that the wound may cause infection of the principal members, it is convenient to apply a light linen cloth soaked in hot poplar oil or rose oil between the angles, and under the joints; and if he feels pain or pus in the bowels, and this happens often, then give him wine vinegar cloves, and similarly when the pus comes from the intestine; and perceive that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "juin" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the power of the veins in it, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and its approach to its own nature from within.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the vein bursts from the wound, then you should put it back again as if it were the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it has become thickened and turned to a black color, it is fitting that you tie the healthy one which is black, for it does not bleed much, because it has veins and arteries; then strike what is between the ligature, and hang the two tendons down from the part underneath the wound until the vein stops bleeding, and the wounds heal.
de la routure dou boueil	of burning with the hot iron
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, so that it can be restored in some people, because I have seen that one man was pierced or stabbed with a lance; and the wound was on his right side under the stomach, and became inflamed and developed an abscess, and in this he had evacuation and vomiting; I treated him according to what I knew, and did not cease to subdue it until he was healed, and the pus dissipated.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him heal, I doubted that the sick had not had illness in his belly; and there was no malady, but he remained in better disposition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he should be bound in such manner: take large straps to big testes, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the strap covers the mouth, put them up on both lips, so that they constrict his mouth again; and then strike the head, and this holds so that he cannot untie it, then put another strap after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and tie the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, and there is no harm to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread that has been cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of that thread of intestine which is much uncleaned, and then tie it to the head of that thread of fine linen twisted, and then pour the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it through; and this method of sewing is not fiery, except according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, just as it is in one of the intestines, there will be no healing or recovery unless with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Things that all wounds or abscesses, when they ulcerate, are universally called "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and has turned purulent.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	Et fistule is according to the hardness of the nodulation of the vein that must be freed from being hard and waxy; or you do not feel pain, and it is like a bird's feather; and sometimes clean bowels, and at other times thick; sometimes little, and at other times enough; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not healed, and there is no discharge, is due to fire only by one of the seven causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the vein or flesh; or because it is malicious; or because of what has caused its hardness inside, and above the lips, that does not allow discharge to occur; or there are too many bowels; or the liver is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because of the corruption which is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late, the digestion is delayed, and the health is late, and it flees by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have shown all these causes, and signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you of the remedy for fistulas which is made by hand work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	There are fistulas that occur in all parts of the body; because there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or from the scrotum, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or on some of the ribs, or to the spine at the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and thus as if they were near a principal part.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas of this kind are a source of disease and suffering, except for labor and ignorance; if there is any fistula that does not appear to be close to its opening when you said so, and you have faith in the cure, and it appears to be working, take a thread or iron rod, depending on whether the fistula is straight or curved; and if the fistula is curved, look for a subtle thread of wood, because the threads stretch through the curvature; and if the fistula has lost hands and you cannot find its opening by thread, wrap it around one of the lost hands, because the moisture is too short from one of the lost hands, and it will be cleaned off; then look carefully with your own skill, to see whether there are bones or nerves, and ask the patient where he feels pain when you press on that spot, and find out where it is; and when you know truly where it is, and whether it is close to a joint, nerve, artery, or vein, or any of the places I have told you about, follow the remedy according to what I have told you, and remove the rotten parts and corrupted flesh that are inside; and then continue with the cure until it is healed, and if the fistula appears straight in front, copy it into its deepest part, as long as you can, and afterwards put moistened threads or medicine on the surface of the fistula, and apply them to the head of the opening, until the excess moisture is corrupted; and afterwards put clean ointments to heal the wound; and if it does not heal by this means, cauterize as we have said, and if the bones are corrupted from the fistula, copy it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	In case of a vein or nerve that is swollen or inflamed, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it until the corruption is completely opened, and then treat the cure with care until it is safe; and if it is not safe, and they bring him back to their former state, you should know that you are not doing well: if you uncover and require it so that you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore it; and if it is such that it is healthy, then it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If it is not so, you should know that the corruption has gone too far, that there is no hope for it: if there is only one source of trouble at nature's site; and if there are small bones corrupted, and you can treat them with pliers, if there is a suitable instrument available to you, and if there are many bones, you should remove all of them; and if moisture is against you, and there is no error or fear, then cut and apply pressure and charcoal, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you cannot remove them in one hour, then place the wound closed and put a dressing to prevent rotting, and leave it until the pus is inside the bones, and then they will have lighter bones; and if this is one large bone such as a thigh or knee, you should only stop the corruption so much that the black color is completely lost from the bone, and then heal the wound; and if there is a great part of the decay, and it comes to a mole on the bone; you must consider and cover all just until the corrosion, and then treat the patient until they are cured; and I will tell you about one case that happened in a man's leg, so that you take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body, until the matter arrived at the leg, and he ran away from a large abscess, and did not have any other reason to open it; but they misjudged by their foolishness so much that they opened the abscesses too much, and they corroded a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came a lot of pus that everyone feared for his health; and many physicians treated him within two years, and there was no solution in the art of hands, until I was called, and I went to see his leg and the medicines they used to treat him, and what corroded by the pus had a great impact on the body; and the young man's skin turned red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I have bounded a tent across one of these holes, and then searched everywhere for the holes, and found that some were coming together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I came back then, and I cut across one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and it was found to be rotten and infected, and it came with infection all around the bone inside; I saw what appeared on the surface of the bone, and I thought that there was no other infection but that which I had taken out; and I began to heal the wound with medicines for a long time, and it would not heal; and then I started again, and I discovered the bone as before, and I found the infection continued in the bone, and I took it out, and I feared to solder it; but I could not do so until I cut across half of the bone, and pulled it out to its full thickness, and then I restored it with medicines; and it became healed and soldered quickly, and it did not require starting again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood is often performed, but it leaves the patient completely healthy, and a hard lump was formed in place of the bone, and he became of good disposition and did not have any hindrance or discomfort whatsoever, neither at rest nor on moving around.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, he will do this: take two ligatures, and tighten them at the head of the bone where it opens up, and command that they stretch upwards; and put another ligature made of a thicker linen over the first one, and tie it above the lump which has destroyed the bone, and set the joint so that you are pulling on the charred part downwards, and uncover the charred part below with your fingers or an awl, until you reach the surface where he is recovering, without blemishing the char; and put a splint or a table under the bone to cover up the corrupting lump; and do so again as soon as it can be seen and felt that there is corruption.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and corruption is in one part or another, so uncover the flesh entirely; then put a tusk under, and then sew from one part to the other the corruption, and sew it with the tissue long of the corruption as we have said; and if corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupted joint, and sew the bone where it contains the other part; and if corruption is in the continuity of two joints, there is no other thing but a covering; and if corruption is at the finger of the hand or at the toe of the foot, it is very strong that place, but you must inquire how the corrosion opens; and make it clean with all sorts of ways possible, but so that the vein or nerve do not turn against you; and learn that the cutter and the sewings for covering these bones are many, according to the seat of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their grandeur and smallness, and their hardness.
dou feu	Fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the joints are swollen or due to infection, and when you have treated that corruption with medicine, and it does not help, then it is advisable to cover up that member until the source of the corrosion, and if the patient escapes from death by means of that corruption, or by the malice of the limb, which is more severe, a failure of the limb; and there are signs such as the members become blackened, so that it seems like they have been burned with fire, and after that blackness, the corrosion spreads to member after member, and takes over all the body; if you hurry to cover, and this is due to the percussion of certain venomous animals, such as scorpions from the sea and lizards and similar ones, when the corruption is at the head of the two, hit them, and do not give them any space before coming close to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Et s'elle vient jusque la main, si la coupe a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne vienne jusque bras; and if it comes just at the hand, so that the cut is on the joint, so that there will be no infection up to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, so that the cut is on the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that's a death, and nothing is useful for fires but the quantity of its virtue; and thus do it whenever corrosion comes on the bone: if it comes to the first joint, so that the cut is after the other joint; and if it comes on the bone, so that the cut all over the bone; and if it rises up in the knee, so that the cut is at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, so there is no other help for the sick man than to kill him with the lagger; and the manner of cutting or wrapping the member is such that you tie it both above and below, and extend one minister over the other, and then serve the cloth which is between the two threads at one span wide, until the bones are exposed; then cut or wrap, and put from each side a piece of linen, so that the cloth does not touch the healthy part, and comes to the sick man another lesion and an abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.
