And the qualities of its suture if are such that the patient will take a bath, and pull upwards from the ankle three fingers, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then suture in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is much harder to tie than to cut.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find it, so healthy any rain on the open or back of the foot, and towards the small toe, and guard yourself from harm; make as much care in the wound that you see, and then release the tie, and put on cotton and bandage; now she is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of wounds caused by suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or thorns, or glass; and suction is done in two manners: either by striking and attracting the wound, or by striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction done by striking is in two manners: either it is with fire on the whole face; or with fire; and suction done by striking and pulling out the wound is made in thirteen places of the body, so that one is on the top of the head; and others are near the neck; and two others on each shoulder; and the ventouse under the chin; and under the elbows; and above the knees; and the ventouses between both arms; and the ventouses on both legs; and the ventouses on both ankles; and this suction does not apply to wounds, unless to small veins scattered throughout the flesh, so that no harm is done, as one makes a vein dressing; and it should not be administered except with fire or by striking, in any disease caused by overfilling, until all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Instruct the patient to let their hair grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it comes to an inflammation of the month, we instruct the surgeon to open the vein after three hours on the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The inflammation of the spleen is most helpful to the coldness of the head … that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this operation is in place of the splenic disease, and should not be used by one with a hot complexion, or who has catarrh, because it causes great harm; and therefore it should not be used by those who are keeping watch, or who have cold head ailments.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from this often become blind, and therefore it should be placed a little lower by the incision for the blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The left side of the neck is in its place at the joint of the shoulder and chest and basilica, and for this reason it is painful to press with the fingers, and breaking open the channel of the arm, and bruising, and swelling; and it should not be pressed too much, because if she holds it too tightly, it causes oblique or stomach pain and to the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosation has two sides of the neck if it causes pains in the head, eye pain and emigraine, and strangulation and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is in place of the basilica; therefore it is necessary to order the lord that he presses his hand on putting, so as not to strike the artery, and wait until blood flows.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Ventosation below the chin causes mouth sickness, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases in the mouth; and is in place of the wounds on both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders value the disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the sides value as much as three veins in the arm, because they cause blood loss from these large veins; and instruct the lord that he should not cut too deeply, for the skin is bare of flesh, and feels pain beneath and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound that is under the buttocks values as much as moroses in the root, and other diseases below, so it's necessary for the wound to be large and filled with earth, because if it were subtle, it would break; and thus makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The wounds of the legs heal largely, because they cause blood loss from all over the body, and are equal to old pains in the rains, and marrs, and bladder, and draw out the flowers; and are like two soles, and two knees, and harm the body after a long time, and make come pale in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	Instruct the patient to put on the ventouse first when empty, and to apply it perfectly, and then have it ready, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the limb red and swollen, and feeling the redness of the wound; then, release, and remove the ventouses, and take care in the arrangement of the dead, because there are such people who have broken bones, and delicate things: if it is necessary to pierce only once, and it is advisable to make large wounds, and a little deeper, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not big, then you must pierce twice: once to subside the large wound.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very thick, then it is advisable to pierce the third time; and when we try to apply a small amount of the wound a little at a time, so that we suffer only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	Instruct the patient if you wish to cut a lot of blood, so frequently bleed again; and if the wound is swollen, then prick it firmly, and the ends are that they will be perceived suddenly, and pay attention to him who has thick skin and hard, and who have many pores, that you anoint them with the oils of olives, dissolving and aperitive: if this is for you, use olive violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it's in yveir, use cresson oil, or lettuce, or camomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If the superfluence is large and cold, take on olive amber oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If the hairs are long and even, do not put point of oil on them; but after the cauterization with rose water, cold water, mulberry water, cucumber water, porcelaneous water, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they raise themselves with rose water of myrtle and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large suppurations, they raise themselves from old wine, cold water of rue, or decoction of anise and camomile, or similar things; and do not want to recover by venesection before the bath or immersion, but after the bath for one hour or two; and do not sleep after the evacuation, and must wait that they can be evacuated, when they need to be evacuated and when they are evacuated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	Instruct the patient who is recovering to be cautious of his temper and if he is not too angry and inflamed; then it is advisable for him to take cold things such as pears, grapes and endives and lettuce at ease, and similar things; and eat pottage, and char broth, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, should take syrup of honey and sweet-smelling wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat pottage, and small fowl and pigeons; and the day before he is going to recover, he must drink more than he eats; and it is advisable to give some people a trifle or muscat wine once in a while before the recovery, or after, for comfort of the main limbs; but be cautious without it, because it is not good that those who are hot should drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles qui sont mises sur le foie et sur la mice, et podagre, et sur le ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sur le ventre et sur la boude pour amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sur le foie et sur la mice quand il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont vuides pour sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes plaines d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cauterizing vessel administered to fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two of equal size and half a palm in depth, and has a groove at the middle with a small hole, as if to put a needle, and is made of wood soft before so that it does not bleed the patient when placing on the member; and has a bar of iron or wood crossed over at the midpoint to hold a bandage, and they are large and small as per the diseases and age of those who take them; for the cauterizing vessels of children are different from those of adults, and small ones are used for thin people, and large ones for fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one must put this cauterizing vessel on the member: take a candle of wax or linen and wrap it around the cauterizing vessel through the bar that is in the cauterizing vessel, so that the light is at the bottom of the cauterizing vessel, so as not to burn the patient; and then place it on the member, with your fingers above the hole we have mentioned, if you wish to let the vapor go out, and when you take away the cauterizing vessel; and wrap on the linen as before, and rewrap often, if need be.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of the patient with pleurisy, who has high fever, he should not have blood or pus, and he should be treated only when he is full of fever, and placed on the limb alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Blood vessels are treated only in limbs where you cannot put a vein, just like nails and gums, and similar ones; and in their nostrils, just like two or nose, and other similar ones; and the quality of the treatment is such that when you find blood vessels that are in pure and clean water without danger, take them; and put one nut in clear water, until they become familiar with it, and have nothing in their stomachs; and then apply vein and vein again, and rub the limb until it's red, and put on the stitches; and when they're full of blood, and swell, if you can put a vein, put it, because this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If it is not so, then lift the limb from the cold and put in warm water, and then try it out; and if the limbs are healthy again after a period of absence, then wet the bandage with cold water and apply it, until they are stanchioned; and if they become swollen many times, then apply vitriol crushed or vinegar, and similar things, until they are stanchioned; or put on the limb half of boiled peels, and leave them until they dry on the limb, so that now it will be stanchioned; and if you have more need, take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the poultices do not take, then rub the limb with fresh poultice, or prick an arrow until it bleeds, and then apply them; and as soon as they feel the poultice, they will dry up; and when you see that they begin to flow, then powder on a little aloes and powdered silver, or ashes, so that they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of a medical book, "The Book of Injuries
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that this art is rarely seen in the writings of the ancients, and they do not read any books or letters on it; and for this reason, the science has been lost in our land, because I did not find a good one anywhere, and I do not know anything, except by the knowledge of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated them with science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described here what is contained, and condensed it in the end, and shown clearly the forms of the fractures, as I did in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in this book's prologue the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise men put their understanding, and keep on with the virtue, so that those who have been proven can learn and acquire this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when any break or dislocation or torsion or swelling comes to anyone, it is necessary to hasten to heal the sick person from one side and from the other, if nothing stops them, such as weakness of the body, or sickness, or old age; or if they are in extreme cold, which is known as frostbitten joints, and charred flesh of birds and deer, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and do not overload themselves with too much meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about an abscess or swelling in the joint; for it is often seen that those who fall ill return to their previous state.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones start to restore, it is fitting that you nourish the patient with foods that cause great swelling, or have viscosity, such as bread cooked in water, and risotto, and testes, and pike, and panca of veal, and oysters, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the swelling is most represented by muscles and more quickly the break occurs.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old and decrepit people cannot be well taken in again or soldered according to their nature because of the drying of the members, nor can those who are too tender, like the bones of small children; but there is no cure. So set large splints on the broken bone, which hold together the member as best it can, until it becomes so that it was before; and do not keep all its work to itself, and for this reason they must nourish with great foods, just as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And knows that fractures are different in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or thigh, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur from a blow to the neck, and others that happen by cutting, just like the length of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture with only a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own tool and instrument for restoration, according to what is remembered in its place; and it's known the fracture of the bone by how the limb is twisted, and opens well when forced, and sounds like a bone when pressed with the finger; but if there's no twisting or sound at the joint, and the patient does not feel great pain, unless there's a point of fracture; but they can still have twisting, a small split, or a slight fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary to move your hand, but apply medicines that come after this, then hold now with subtle restraint.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that when a break occurs in the arm, and the two joints are separated, it is now necessary to put them back on an even basis, so that they do not form abscesses; and if abscesses form there, let one day pass, until they are healed; then put it back on the joint that you can easily feel, and know that the restoration of the other part is lighter than the restoration of this one where pieces remain; then hold, as it should be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and you feel two parts, it is either with a large piece or with your hand, or with small members, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; then put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the injured limb are diminished, you restore them through all kinds of means on the joint that you can feel, and avoid that by your work the patient suffers a new injury or pain; and add well both joints of the bones in their best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to you that he is not at all: if the dress is done perfectly, and is not strained too much, nor pressed like those who are doing this because of their own work, with pain and contraction on the member, as we have often had.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is fixed, instruct the patient well so that it does not move, nor watch, nor sleep, nor turn, nor in any other way; and carefully take care that the limb be so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	But when he feels no pain, it is not fixed, and you must take care to put him in a certain disposition so that he does not feel any pain; and carefully guard that he be placed correctly, lest twistedness comes upon him when restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The body parts that break are diverse in size, shape, and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For the small members, such as fingers and toes: it is necessary to wrap them with soft linen drapes; and for those that are large, like knees and legs: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and sturdy rope. For the large ropes embrace the entire limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no breakage. Then tie over gentle wraps, three or four according to the member, and tighten your hand on the rope, then go up to the top of the fracture and loosen it a little, so that the fracture will move slightly. And gradually loosen the rope, so much that you take hold of a large part of the healthy limb; then put on another rope, and turn back over the break; then return below the break, and loosely tighten, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first sentence above; then place linen or drapery wraps between the ropes, until it is entirely equalized; then tie everything from above with a bandage, and then put your splints well made on top, if there is an abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if it has an inflammation or abscess, put on soothing ointment to the inflamed place, and who operates on the inflammation, let it remain for some days; then strain over those wounds, and sew with a chain rope of one-fifth width, or a log used for cleats, or palm wood, and according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the chain rope which one puts on the breakage be slightly larger and wider than the others; and so long as it suits the limb of small or large size; then bind over those wounds just as you have done at the first suture, then tie above with a flexible thread, just as in the first suture on the breakage; tighter is above, softer below; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, not too thick or too thin, and made of linen yarn; for if the thread are too big, as I wanted to do my work done by the foolish ones who make their sutures with cordage of fine linen twisted, and this is a great error, because the suture cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it does not suit that there be less than two fingers' breadth between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sick from the stings of these arrows after stretching in their strength, then they must apply ointment of linen or wool to stop the bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the tendons are broken, I will tell you the cure as follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to strain the entire limb every time with a fracture on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to apply arrows on every member every time with a fracture; but after 4 or 7 days, or more according to the swelling of the abscess present at the site; and here I will tell you the manner of the ancient apothecaries for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsion: that you take flour kept in the walls of the mill, and mix it with a great quantity of fat, and make this confection, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and it is the common way of restoring fracture at more than one disposition; and myself, as well as women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to restore the break and dislocation and twisting: take 12 grains of lead arsenic and ladanum and oroside and asafetida and gum arabica and muga, ana X; myrrh and aloes, ana V; alechil VIIII; and make a powder, and mix with honey with a little wine; if the complexion of the oil is hot, use this ointment because it is of good composition, and restores the broken bones quickly, and saves more men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to oint that is for twisting: take muga and visnalmum, ana X; myrrh and aloes, ana VIIII; camphor VI; boric of Armenia X; grind well, and confine with water or a little wine, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to treat a joint and bone separation, remove the joints and bones from their place, and ease the pain that follows, and use the bone to mend it: take new linen, apply oil easily in hot water, and put them back in place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plaster dressings do not restore the joint, but they are good for soothing an abscess and properly treating pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat a fractured bone that restores the bones: take dry fig leaves and earthly leaves, crush them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat plaster for restoring the fracture of the bone and to alleviate the swelling of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Pick the root of wormwood, camomile, violet flowers, flour of vine, one part from each; and grind, and mix with wine, and apply to the members while they are heated, or mix with moist coriander water, or water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of applying plaster more forcefully than the first, when an abscess hardens at the restoration of a limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Pick the root of wormwood, and the seed of flax, balsam, melilot, and sanssouci, and violet flowers and camomile flowers, each one a part; grind, and mix with salty water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Iporcras says in his book that you should not put on the broken limb a plaster made of wax and oil alone, but rather something more, and he says it should be neither too dry nor too moist.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that we must place a poultice on the broken limb, to restore health, dry things made warm, like mirrors and alum and incense, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat the wound and pain: take meat and horsehair of a dead man, or bird quills, and vinegar, and make it equal in size, break it up, and make an poultice with the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then wait a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that their bone is out of place; if it does not come back in its place by hand, or if they have pain, swelling or redness, if you hasten, and remove it, and now apply the poultice again; and take a light bandage, and a sponge soaked in moist water, and plunge in the water, and lift up the limb, until the itching stops and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, and put on a dry linen, moistened with water or oil rose, and tie it over a nut, until you are sure that the abscess has healed; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and allow the pain to cease, then resume gentle movements, and apply a poultice again, and do not strain it too much as before; and be gentle until it is sound.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess has chaus and is red and painful and swollen, I have set a bone there to make it whole again, and you must apply plaster and bind it, if it swells again, as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if this does not come to the limb as we have said, then do not unbind it for more than three or four or five days, and never let it remain for twenty days, according to what is seen, until the fracture heals, and approaches the joint near; then tighten it even more than before, and feed its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see that it dries out more than needed, know that swelling cannot come from it; therefore take care of it with hot water and vinegar every time you unbind it, and do this on the tenth day, and a little later. By this work, then cut off the swelling from the limb, and make haste to apply what the foolish doctor does, which will remain in the limb twisted: that is bad, and if it is done badly, I see no other thing but that of binding and overdoing it straightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of breaks
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of breaks, and various forms, and the causes are determined; for there are fractures that are made by the force of a sword, and the cartilage is broken all along with the bone just beneath it, like a blow or a punch; and thus this kind of fracture is called «haichure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword strikes the bone on both sides to pierce it, and this is called a fracture «absolue», because of the two wounds resulting from these two fractures whether large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has penetrated deeply into the bone, or is a split, or breaks through the joint of a stone, or pierces above the stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persisting fracture, which approaches just beneath the skin or above the bone, or it is this wound that is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is covered with bone as thin as our nails, and there are small splits, and because of this they call this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by hitting a stone, or falling, or some similar thing, and pushes a piece of bone into the body, and the little hairs (chevez) become as when the blacksmith heats over the fire when he heats his bellows; so there goes in the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones in their head, as when they are children; and it happens in all these kinds of fractures where small pieces come out like stones. And I will speak about them on his behalf.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by removing them, and inquiring about them, and by the corrupting flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The shape of the hair is known by this: when you have discovered the bone and rubbed above it, if you open the dark fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of any accidents that occur to the patient, and if you do not see any bad accidents, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, pale skin, fever, eyes protruding and turning red, and other similar dispositions, then it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any extraordinary accidents, and you expect good health, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the arm comes to you first, and it is in winter, it is fitting to remove the bone on the 14th day before the full moon when you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, so that you hasten to remove the bone on the 7th day, then thus the skin under the bone will be corrupted, and accidents will come as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break in the bone comes just next to the covering of the brain, it is fitting that you split the fractured part thus: and that you take the patient's head into your hands, and uncover under the bone in all ways as you can, and on the face of the wound as soft as you can, and if blood comes when uncovering the bone or abscess, or if you help with whatever is necessary, then it is that you fill the wound with moist cloth soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess subsides, and be sure to avoid the occurrence of bleeding; then begin under the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two kinds of work: one way is that you cut straight at the trimming beforehand, and it is like this:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then pour another, more extensive cutting than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of various cuttings, some three-pointed and others long, all of iron, and work lightly so as not to hit the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, so it's fitting that you pierce into it, otherwise, you administer cuttings with saws, not because you will break through the bone at once, but rather so that the point does not pass beyond the softest part of the bone, and has a margin or circle above the point, so that the point doesn't go through beyond the bone; and it's fitting to have more than one, so each one comes in its own time, like the growth of the bone under the saw; and this is the form of the three kinds of saws:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the bone when it is broken are that you will set up a tarry (a piece of bone or metal) on top of the bone, and turn to your two hands until you know that the bone has been pierced; then remove the tarry to another place after a little while, and do so all around, then strike at the incisors with the space between the pertus (the points of the bone), and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you retrieve the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have, such as tongs, pincers.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and extracted it, if there remains something stuck to the bone that has not been freed from the other instruments resembling an incisor, but is more subtle and finer than the others; and if it adheres nothing at all to the small bones or scales, so that the bone can be easily taken away with any instrument; then treat the wound as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of opening is such that the Gauls say, which is more so; and it's said very loudly, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary to uncover a part of the bone, on one side or where the break opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will put below the head of this incision, lens-shaped, because it is this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not strike from one side, and the part is located in both sides, so that the striking is towards the bone; then with a small hammer above, so that you carefully copy the bone all around, and protect yourself well from the cloth that is below; if it is rough against the bone, carefully remove the bone, because you must carefully remove the bone without pain or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone is not pierced through to the fabric, and the bone is merely hit from above, with small pieces, it should cover up that roughness, and remove the scaly skin at a subtle razor that you must have in various quantities, so that each patient has the most comfortable fit, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have many coarse razors, and after that more subtle ones, and do not cease to do this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other small hair-cutting and fracture treatments, it is convenient to adjust according to its intention; and this is a thing that cannot be found in one who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the sinew is uncovered, it is convenient to tie off a linen cloth, according to its quantity, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another linen cloth doubled twice or three times, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first one; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not press too hard on the sinew, but only until the wound begins to heal; and leave it for one day or two, until the inflammation is subsided, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour of wheat, incense powder, and aromatics, and similar things; and make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer after medicines with mastication; and be careful that the wound is completely healed, so that you do not leave any swelling or assemble any bowels, for when bowels are assembled over the brain cloth, they burst and cause great suffering to the patient; because when something sharp is placed over a wound, it burns from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no other accidents come to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful and full of doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not happen fire because of the medicine that has been placed on him, which has its virtue, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and glue one sheet, and put it on the wound; then apply the cure in ways of cures until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two lower bones are broken, or one alone, because they are two bones; and this one is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, it is convenient that you pour your little dough or paste on the bone, and put this break inside your dough index, and in a pouchet because of, until the bone regains its natural shape; do this gently, and take care that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is above the neck, and it cannot come to rest in its place, then you must put equal to the head of a stick one little bit large.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the break is in two parts, do it again, and hasten to restore it the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or fifteenth day, when the wound has healed, then wrap the head of the neck with linen cloths, if the break is in a part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you put another cloth on the other part, if the break is there; and the cloths be so thick that they fill the holes in the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said no restorer that "we must moisten the cloths in butter, and move each one every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I don't understand the prompt.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes pour out the blood of an owl in place of poultices, and if it's wrapped around a wound, and kept still, blow air into the patient; then let go what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	If an abscess comes out while you're working on it, apply a dressing of rose oil or cotton soaked in oil and vinegar, or a poultice made from the root.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess does not come out, apply an emplaster made from wheat flour and incense powder mixed with rose oil, then put on light stones, and do not tie the wound; if the fracture is small and it's broken into little pieces, take out what can be extracted, then sew the cut, and treat wounds as needed, and cauterize, just like emplasters and ointments. And if there is no injury inside the abscess, apply poultices, and put in clean gauze, until it's healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	About the cutting of the jawbone.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is cut below and there is no wound to prevent it, and only a clean break without any splitting, whether in flesh or bone, if one notices that it is slightly broken.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right hand side, to put your right index finger into the patient's mouth; and if it is in the left jawbone side, then put your right index finger in your left hand, and put the break inside lightly, and press on the other hand without any further care, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is split in two, it is necessary that you provide extension of both parts, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth occur, or a breakage, then tie up with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and put on the broken mandible coteh (cotton), and put on the double drapel (cloth); and put on the double drapel an estele good made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the mandibule, and tie it up with what you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light viandes.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, if you let it go for three days, and then put back what is changed; and apply plaster on it, with powder of the mill with a lot of water or flour of silk, after you have removed the cotton; and put on the plaster linen light, and if the plaster hardens, and the disposition of the patient does not change, let him be so long until he is healed; many are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If there is an abscess on the foot, do so as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If there is a break and wound together, repair no piece of bone if it has been removed; for a subtle method with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, then enlarge it as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have removed all those pieces and there is no remaining bone, then close the wound if it is large; and put on suitable plasters to keep it clean, until he is cured.
de la forcele	of the wrist.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The wrist breaks often in front of the shoulder, and there are three kinds of fractures: or it is broken and separated into two, with pieces, and is lighter to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the wounds are thus when the break is felt at the injury, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder where the force breaks; and the other stretches out the neck towards the part; then place the break on your two hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there be no appearance or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have need to stretch more, place a round spear of cloth or linen on the patient's shoulder, so that it is as big as your necessity requires; and extend and lift the skin, and hold tight the spear with your hand, so that you put the break in its proper place.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot treat the head of the swell with caution, because it is coming out in full, then it is fitting that the patient should lie on his hat; and place a cushion under the shoulder, and pour the ministers the shoulder down, until the bone of the swell rises.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the break to your two joints, and if you find that it is fractured, so be it that you cut it; and take out the pieces lightly, and if the bones cannot join for any swelling, so strike at one of the incisions that you have; but put on the force of this instrument, to ward off the syphilitic.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not of wood, and so large as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and has two handles, if you see, and one broad, and the other narrow, just like the routuring of the wound that you made when you cut the bones; and when you are sure about the abscess deep, then close the wound, and if the routuring is small, or you doubt the abscess is deep, then apply the wound with draperies and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms on the foot, apply a poultice of melted oil, rose petals, and ash, and place it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is painful and swollen, is to place the bone on poultice made from flour of the mill and ale yeast, with light cloths above, and fix with nails below if necessary; then take a great bandage of a palm in width, and put a poultice double above the cloths, and then take a small needle three fingers long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the head of the bandage is hanging; place the needle on the break, and turn the bandage over the shoulder, and under the armpit, and under the side of the sick person, and pull from each part, and when you see that the limb holds the break in place immediately, and you see clearly that the needle does not move above the broken bone, then reward one for every day, and when the ligature is set, fix it; and have the patient lie on his back, and under the armpit put a small oil cloth below the shoulder, to lift the support up high; so he will be cured by the tightening of the shoulder or by binding the arm to the neck, in 20 days; then reapply the poultice if you see that it is needed, and fix it and leave it thus, until he is restored; and he is restored in 28 days, and for few people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	From the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It is often that the shoulder breaks or widens when it does not heal through touch; if you arrange according to the shape of the break and its natural form, in all kinds of ways as you can; then put powder from the mill with much oil and light cloths on the patient, and place an iron bar double; then place a large iron rod, slightly larger than the shoulder, and smooth it out over every inch of the shoulder so that the iron rod is evenly smoothed; and then tie it firmly to one end of the bandage, so that the iron rod does not move from its place, and look at the patient each day; and every time he swallows, tighten the bandage, and put the iron rod in its proper place, if it is out of place, and rest the patient on his chest; and the shoulder will heal in XX days or XXV, And when these numbers are completed, you can release him, and be certain, for it is not that he puts on flesh lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a piece of bone is protruding and not beneath the surface level, do thus, and lift the skin, and take out the bone, and do as we have said in the breaking of the abscessed tooth.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	But it is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely, and it breaks often without reason.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, so that one side is lower than the other, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of appetite, and swelling, and sometimes vomiting blood, and opening up the veins on the broken bone, and the wound opens well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.
