And the restoration is done so that the patient lies on his back, and you place a cloth between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the two breastbones with your hands, and subtly put in order all sorts of things until the figure of the bone becomes as it should; then place plaster and poultices over the subtle part of salt, or another lighter substance, and tie it around the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the knot round to the back, and tighten immediately, and reward each hour the bandage, and if it loosens, re-tighten it; and if it is loosened because of corrosion or itching that comes to him, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and untie it, and shave the plaster, and direct the things that are coming back by such cures; then remove the plaster, and tie it again until he becomes healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	This breaks only when the ribs are large behind the back, and in the chest area, and they collapse because they are crooked; and it hurts very much at the inquiry of these places.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatments are such that you put equal the break, as it is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster, and bind with a stick, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the ribs break inward, it causes the patient great pain, and sticking, like of pleurisy, because the bone punctures the membrane; it makes pain, swelling, and vomiting, and a great amount of bloody discharge, and this is a sign of ill health, and the old ones used to put much effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say it should be given foods that swell the belly, to beat down the break in safety.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless an abscess has formed on the flesh.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that you should put bellows on the limb to suck out the flesh, as it seems reasonable; all ways, there is doubt that the bellows does not attract the excesses to the limb by weakness of disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that you should cover the limb with a linen cloth soaked in hot oil, and put towels between the ribs to make the joint even, then treat with the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient if they feel great pain because of a bone that presses on the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is advisable to break open the swollen part of the fractured rib, and it is advisable to put some instrument under it to ward off the abscess; and thus one must dig into the bone, and treat lightly, and then sew the two sides of the wound, if it is large, and cure with plaster, until they are sane.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess comes on the limb, put up moist drapes in olive oil on it, and place the limb; cure while the limb is swollen to the degree that it needs incising, and let it swell more on the rib where it should be, until they are sane.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is no break when the bone of the neck breaks, and it does not collapse; and likewise at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens and you see that it will be either cured or not cured, if you prepare yourself to see whether your hands are swollen, inflamed, and dead, and cannot move or stretch, and when you press them with a needle, they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Recognize that it is mortal in more difficult cases, and if they are mute and feel well when you press them and pinch, recognize that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient is cured, provided that someone puts them on treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if such a thing happens at the spine of the back, and you see whether it will be cured or not, if you prepare yourself, if the feet are softened, and if the accident is severe in the hands, and on the back there is great movement and evacuation with a strong desire, and when one gets wind of it upon its belly, it moves with a strong desire.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to get up, then he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Knows that it is mortal if he does not work on his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this injury did not happen to him, then the condition is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the doctor says that if he has an abscess hot and puts oil of rose or oil of rye flour on it until it is appeased; then puts on a comfortable dressing and bandages with a tie, commands the patient to rest; and does not lie on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is shattered, it is proper to cover over the wound; and cut off the bone, then put together the two lips of the wound, if they are large, with a seam, then treat the wound with binding linen wrapped around charcoal, until he is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "chiés de la kowe", put your left pocket hand in it, and put it even on the other hand to your power, then put on dressing and splint if necessary; then bind it, and if there is a bone shattered, they make it straight, cut off, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the shinbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the shinbone is fractured, and if it has, then if it was not even slightly alleviated at first; and let it be long, and decline to the padded side; and comes to the patient pain, point, and swelling, as if the break.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you stretch out your hand above, until you are on top of the fracture; and see which way the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only in the head alone, then straighten up this fracture, so long as it returns to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it inclines inward, then have the patient lie on his stomach, so that the restoration of this fracture becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have straightened it so that it is even, put on the plaster cast, then put on a splint of wood or of horn, and tie up the break, so that it does not move; and apply plaster under the bones, so long as they are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his sound side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes on to the foot, do not touch it, until the abscess is opened and applied to what we have said before; and then come back to restoration, and bind as is necessary, without any further injury; for this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The joints are that which is between the shoulder and the head of the shoulder; and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two methods: one being that you take a strip of linen cloth as thick as a middle-sized twig, in this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And let the two thumbs be put on either side of the joint, and point upwards, and sit the patient on one siege; then sit the gaiter over the broken arm on the body, until it comes to its place, and has a bone in the same position, then point up at any heavy thing or the ministers extend it downwards; then put the fingers into the breakage equal to his hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is that you sit the patient on their hateryle, and tie the hand to the neck; then command two ministers that one holds what is above the breakage with his hands, and the other holds below all the joints, and extend each of them to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then tighten all the joints below and above the breakage, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	In case of a fracture near the shoulder joint, it is advisable to place one straight band below the bone, and another over the shoulder, below the fracture; and similarly, if the fracture is towards the shoulder, it is advisable to place one lighter band slightly above labor, until the fracture is even on both sides, and on the bone, then set the fracture as needed, and bind so that abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If abscesses come, do not bind them for just 7 days, and place a moist linen in a quiet and oil-soaked basin until the abscess is calmed; then bind, and the manner of binding itself is that you put tallow on the fracture, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and place a bandage, and bind above the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm is in its proper position, unless some thing prevents it, or if the bone is moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bones do not move, then use estesles, and place one larger and stronger than the others on the break, and have two spans of space between each estele, and so that each estele is as big as it passes three spans of each part; then pull tight on the estesles, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the position of the estesles and the straining, as we have said, in the wound where you restore the injured limb, and you doubt whether there is an abscess swelling inside, if you leave it bound for five days, as we have said; then examine each one of those three days the bond, to see if it prurites or swells, or comes a new swelling on the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it happens, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if such accidents do not happen, then let it be only after three days or more, and the patient lies on his back, with his hands under his stomach; and applies to the affected part one cussin plain of equal flax, and looks at each hour, day or night, whether the figure of the broken limb does not move, or does not loosen the ties; for it will come to him by virtue of medicine, and give him the meat that we have put before him, in a manner so that the meat is first tenderized; and when he begins to recover, if it becomes thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be returned to their place after forty days in full; and therefore, one must dislocate and administer bath and medicine for relief of the pain.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is tight and blocked, so it stays open for one or two days.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fossicle", for because one is small, and that is the one that forms the pouch; and the other is large, and it is below, towards the little bone; by chance only the large fossicle breaks alone, or the small one, and by chance they break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, restoration is light, and healing; and when the large bones are broken, it is poor healing, and they become more grievous than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that was broken alone, then they must take care to extend it lightly, and put it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If it is the large frostbile, then they should stretch it more forcefully; and stretch up to the cussin, and lift the pouchet of the hand higher than the others, and move the fingers lower than the others, so that the patient crosses his own hands on him, and the cussin in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no labor; then extend the minister's some arms to the part below at his hand, or at its tie, and one other minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the fingers equal, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are pieces, then put each one in its own place, and if there is no matching joint that can hold its shape, and you cannot restore it to its proper place, then pull out the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If the wound has an opening, I have mentioned it to the singular surgeon; so take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	If in the beginning of restoration it happens that there are openings (abscesses) in the chest, then apply a cloth made of cerote fat mixed with oil rose and white beeswax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft; and tie the cloth on top subtly until the abscesses have been calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then apply the cerote, and put on the plaster made of powdered flour with a great amount of fat, until the stitches are set in place, and one is slightly more firm, and a little wider than the others; and observe that it should have six stitches or more in good dispositions: whether the break is in one bone, or two; and pull up tighter above the break than elsewhere, always less when you take away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and so that the dressings on top of the break be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the threads, from which it is strained, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the joint after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident happens to the member, just like when it pricks and comes into contact with the member, then it is fitting that you apply a warm bath to the member until the prickling stops; and do not let the member be too constricted.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the straining, and when the ligaments are softened and the bone is removed, and it seems so, direct.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you can't get rid of the swelling in the member because it is too constricted, then it is fitting that you soften it a little and let it stay for some time, until the swelling clears up, and then you strain.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things happen to the patient, as we have said, so that he will not be relieved after twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And after that, you tie the hands to his neck, and make sure they are even, and keep them from movement and from twitching, and he lies on his back; and know that this break is restored in thirty days or forty-five, or perhaps twenty days, according to the humors and the constitution of the person.
de la brisure de la main	of a broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and in our treatment there has been little bruising, except for pleurisy many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plantar part of the hand is broken or sprained, if it pleases, the patient should cross his arms and sit straight in front of him equally; then he puts his hand on an outstretched table, and extends the broken bone, and sets the joints equal to each other until they are well fixed; and applies plaster and pads, unless there is an abscess, then he puts a stake according to its quantity; and if it is not inflamed by 10 days of linen bandage.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	In case of a fracture in the finger joint, inside the palm of the hand, do this: make a splint out of cloth and command the patient to wrap it around his broken finger; then tighten the bandage for a long time, so that the nail is as thick as the finger itself, and tighten, if needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the thumb, so that it should be straight and right, then put a splint on top, and another below the palm, so that the hand is covered and straight, then bind everything around the hand, and tie the ligament between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes from one of the fingers, and it's a thumb, then put an equal dressing on it, as needed; bind with the palm, and if you see, place a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in another finger, such as the index or other, put an equal dressing on it, and tie with the healthy joint that follows; or tie both of them together, until it heals, or put up a splint, as needed; take care in restoring and arranging the abscessed place, and heal who comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	The head of the broken femur
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the broken femur is often fractured and can be seen when it turns in front and behind; and healing like this is as one ties to the above fracture, and to the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patients lean on their face, then stretch each one's limb equally; and this is when the fracture is healed into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the femur, then it has one of the ligaments near the joint, and the others below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, and then so either there are ligaments near the joint, or extension below; then put on the mirels the bone equal to its two hands, as much as is according to its natural figure, and then apply the plaster, and the ligament, so that abscesses do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if it has an abscess, let him calm it afterwards and return to his work and care; the remedy is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap a bandage above the fracture, two or three fingers thick, and hold in place the swelling, then turn the leg until the toes reach the root of the nail, and pour one long thread between the thigh and the knee, tied under, and hang down the heel to the top; then turn up the knee and on the thigh the bandage, then apply plaster to the fracture, and put a stone on the bone of the knee; then put soft draperies between the leg and the knee to equalize the compression, then begin to tie in three turns or four above the fracture; and as you go higher up the fracture, the tighter it will be; then take out with two fingers that thread which you have poured between the thigh and the knee, and put in three stones on top, then return to below to the heel of the foot until you see through the bone; and if the straitening does not move from its place, then let it go, and when it no longer comes with swelling or inflammation or any other appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens again, and the dislocation occurs, and address it as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that hold tight, then they must be removed, if one can; and if one cannot, then must break the limb, and pull out the foreign object; and the cure is done as we have said, until it is whole.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no one is broken like this when setting arrows, just as in the shoulder and arm; it all works out in the restoration done so that the patient has no pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is known that the shoulder is restored in three days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the elbow joint.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	She looks at it and sees a small break, but she bends over many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if she breaks, it is only a crack or a puncture, and she has great pain, and feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is thus: to put equal that which is broken into its two parts, until it is assembled; then apply ointment, and if necessary, put an oval-shaped stone on it; so tie it as it should be tied; then follow all the dispositions that we have mentioned regarding other breaks, as for abscesses and suchlike symptoms; thus put to each one who needs it what you think is required, until they are well.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg break
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	If two bones are in the leg, so that one is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile", and all other fractures occur when it comes to the arm, then the restoration is done equally as the arm, and all the wounds are the same. And if the two bones are broken together, turn the leg from all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bones are broken, then turn in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, then it feels a great pain, and one sees it well; and turn below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And then make an extension, and place it equally; but pay attention, if the break is ugly, and there are more pieces, it is better to have the extension smaller and lighter; and fix according to its value.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et when you have completed all your work, so take two firm sticks which prick the inner and outer part of the leg on one side and on the other, and let them be long from the knee to the toes; then bend over them both above and below, and tie with a bandage around the middle, so that the leg cannot move from right to left or from left to right, and thus it is done well; and no one applies short sticks to the length of the leg, and if they do, and tie them on, and put on the stick for holding still movement, and properly made in the break where it has been injured; and move each person every day the leg, to see if there is a seeping abscess or any other accident; and so the doctor until he is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone break of the foot.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	There is no break at the ankle, but sometimes there are breaks in the lower leg bones and sometimes there are difficulties. There is no need for more than two kinds of dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the lower leg bones, and you see these bones overlapping one another, so put this patient on their foot on the ground, just as they would walk, and then put now your foot on theirs, where the bone is lifted, press it until they align with their own; then apply plaster and strips, and place a small wooden table on, under the belly of the foot, two wooden pegs fixed, then tighten to the foot in order, and other things that you may have need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, release the bandage, because you will find that the bones are even, either broken, or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	Et s'il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j'ai dit, et l'estrain avenanment; et s'il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantitee, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sur lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu'il le teigne bien.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is to be remembered that you should not forget the other things I have told about other breaks, since we have said them before. And then treat each accident as it seems fitting.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone at the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman breaks, if it is set in an enlarged position, then incline it to the back part of the back, and hold it behind; then fill the bag with the nature of the sick person's cotton, and put into it as much as I said; then push down the woman, and lift up her back a little at a little, and thus blow cotton into the nature, until it comes to its opening, and returns to the bone with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, if the cotton obstructs, and when she has urinated, take it away, and do this seven times or more: then will be restored the break, and you see, take a vessel of wool, and tie it to the puncture a cord, and pour the whole vessel into the nature; then blow through the cord until the vessel is gone in: the nature will return the break; then fill with cotton, and leave it thus for some days, till it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the thumb, or in a woman, is broken, as we have said about the bone of the hazelnut; and these nearby breaks are not hidden from one who examines with study and experience, and senses my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	But this break signifies more deaths on the right path of restoration: then therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the vagina, when it is broken, take an owl's gizzard and swallow it into the vagina; then wrap a cloth around it, and let him stay three days or longer, and he will be cured quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for him who has a break with wound, especially if it is great, as with the bone of the shoulder or of the arm, or similar things, to be cured immediately, so that the cures we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the wound is clean, then if it heals again with vitriol, and you have nothing else, then start to restore the break in the same hour, or the next day, unless an abscess forms on your feet.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess on your feet comes up, then delay the restoration to the next day at noon, until the abscess is healed, and do not touch or apply anything to it for three days or four days, lest you bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the broken bone appears near the heart that is discovered, it is to your advantage to put it at a light touch with your fingers slightly bent.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the extension is not fitted for putting equal pressure with your hands, then if it has an iron instrument that is seven or eight fingers long, and the handle is of the size of the wound; and because of this it is the master's task to press three or four, according to what he needs in each wound; and let there be small and a little big, so it does not bend under compression on the limb at your work, and let it be in front, and big from the middle towards in front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the curved head needs to be placed on top of the cheekbone; and the cup should be applied once, until it returns, and the one side against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the splints cannot properly grasp the bone, it is necessary to copy the cheekbone itself, so that the splints will have a chance.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you are unable to return the bone as we have said, if you copy it with a suitable instrument, such as a knife or saw, then take what remains in the bone of roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, you must know that he is not in his natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it happens so that he is in his own place, then cut off the nail on the finger in wine of vinegar black, and properly clean it; and do not put anything else on the wound except oil, lest it bring rotting and corruption; then administer ointments when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the whole covering with stitches according to the size of the wound, and do well to guard that the wound is not tightened with the break; and many times the foolish healer has done this, and has brought death or rot on the patient one time, or corruption; and so the more gentle and softer restraints than the others breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is severe or large, and you doubt that more accidents will not occur, as we have said, and if you find pain in the limb, it does not suit to put on stitches; but instead, cover it with hard bandages, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two the arrow has been tied up to the wound, so that what you have placed above on wine, and I apply salve for healing wounds, just like perfumed ointment and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is fitting that you loosen the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is softened and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is fitting that the limb be bound in such a way that the arrow falls away lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day it transpires and the limb cannot close but again bends, seeing that there are small pieces of bone, for this reason you should consider applying a poultice to the wound, and remove all these superfluous things that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If a fistula comes to the leg, or another kind of corruption, it is advisable that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens in the limb, like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar bones of the great limbs, if you do not treat it, for many times death comes from this, but does not come until he perishes; perhaps he will die after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if you can; if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of wounds that come from a fall onto the soft earth
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	These come many times after the health of the fracture, especially when it's near a joint, and one sees the poor figure of the limb; and by chance the limbs cannot do their natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Pren ward donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d'uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l'estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu'il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l'oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu'ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu'ele soit sanee.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	One weak member after the castle
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored and stays after the weak members and subtle ones, such things happen: because one of them occurs because he was tied too tightly, and wasn't tied as it should have been; or because there are too many ties, and can't come to the member; or for many arrowings; or for great movements, not in his hour; or because he has little blood in his body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the patient eat, and make his body soft, until there are no more arrows in him; then administer baths, and give joy and delight; afterwards put poultice on the member, so that the poultice attracts great swelling, and often draws out water from it, until the swelling comes to the member; and returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	One tortured member after the sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after healing, and the bones are fractured, and the form of the member is deformed, it is useless to attempt its natural movement; nor should you believe false doctors who say one must break the limb anew, for many fools have done this in our land; and such operations are blameworthy, and they bring great harm and even death by chance. Therefore, if the nodations and tortures are fresh, it is best to apply the heat of hot water, or to cook with mellow herbs, such as valerian, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make the patient take a mollifying treatment, just like quinine does well; and take the muscillaige of valerian, and conflate it with lard or sesame oil, and apply it; or take figs greased, and grind them with fine flour of rye, and similar medicines that calm the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And there are times when the node is removed by constant friction and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	and move it every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is old and hardened, like stone, and needs to be set with iron, so that it covers just on top of the bone, at the subtle incision lightly; and apply a cushion and study in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if you want to now bring back into its place carefully.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For when it is late, if the swelling increases, and by chance it is set back on its place; for this reason you should not move it until it subsides: many times it has come to bring spasm and other pains; at any rate, when it happens, cure the patient, then let him go, as long as the pus is brought down; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then move it lightly, and cure each limb as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have instructed the chapter on dislocations of the head, at a price.
des mandibules	of the jaw bones.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	But this happens when the jaw bones are dislocated together, and there are two kinds of dislocations: either they are a little osteoporotic in their place, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down towards the chin, and obstruct the saliva from the mouth so it cannot be held back, nor can the lips be closed, and the tongue is blown out with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to its place through more movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and completed, it is advisable to reduce it immediately, and do not delay; and in such a manner that the ministers will put the chief of the patient on their knees, and pour a small amount of powder from one of its hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation extends up to two parts; and the other two fingers should be avoided for the purpose of putting it equal; and instruct the patient to release his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he puts it equal, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns with wounds, especially when both jaws are assembled, apply hot water and oil, so that the reduction is done lightly; do not delay to reduce it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, and the mouth of the sick person closes well with softened flesh, so put soft, moist cloths in cerote made of oil and wax upon it; and lightly bind them with melted fat ligaments; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his limbs be between two cushions, so that he does not move neither his right arm nor left arm, nor does he try to force himself to make a fist, but takes light meat, until the pains are gone, and the mandibles are stiffened, and then gently bring what he wants to eat, and do not work on opening the mouth to drink and to burp, until the mandible is well hardened and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be brought to a point in one hour and are not converted to their place, then fever and cough come, and sometimes abdominal pain, and sometimes vomiting of solid food.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see that, then know it's a death sentence; and many have died in seven days.
de la forcelle	of the forearm.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forearm cannot be dislocated along the spine or towards the belly, and is displaced only once by force, and it hurts a great deal.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And restoration is that the patient rises onto his back and stretches out his arms; then presses the wound to the palm of his hand, and it heals; then puts on a plaster and bandage, and tightens it; and the joint that was towards the shoulder cannot be dislocated; unless not, and if it is displaced once, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then put on a plaster and bandage, and tighten it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus same is restored of the spine when it is set straight.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three kinds of dislocation of the shoulder: one where it slips below the joint, another where it slips under the arm, and occasionally where it pops out above, this happens rarely; it never occurs behind the shoulder or within the joint, and frequently slips below towards the joint, especially in those who have little strength, because they can hardly withstand it; in those who have strong muscles, it slips with more pain, and returns to pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some people that they hit or bruise the shoulder so hard that an abscess forms, and they believe it is a dislocation.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must examine it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known about dislocations when it occurs near the axilla, and makes a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their diversity manifest; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and below the axilla at the top of the shoulder, as if it were two; and the patient cannot return his hand to its place, nor move from any movement; and thus, if it is displaced upwards, it is not hidden, because you will find manifestly at the shoulder joint; and this manner of dislocation is not hard to treat when new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift up the hand of the sick person above, then put your fingers under the axilla, and lift the joint at force in above towards the healthy shoulder; and the minister lifts up the hand, and extends it upwards, since it has gone down; if this happens suddenly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’ils soient longs et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’ils naissent.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too light, he will lift with him anything heavy, and dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And another way to fix it is to push a long iron rod into the ground, so that the joint moves just like when one is pressing with one's fist, and is neither too big nor too small; then put on top of the patient, but only if he has relaxed somewhat under the heavy stick; then extend his hand in another direction, forming, and the joint will return to its place immediately; and if it does not return for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take an iron rod from two arms of great length and four fingers of width, which has the head just right for entering into a hole deep under the heel, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Instruct the patient to place the head under the weight of a folded stick, so that it does not break, then put the bone of the patient under the bone; and stretch out both arms above the fist, and fix the aid on the arm, and the hand to the top of the shoulder, then put the arm over the joint of one side, and let the limbs hang down from the other part: the joint is now fixed in its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done in any way, so that you should put the bone under one side of a sparrow's feather, then put the plaster on paraffin powder with vinegar and beeswax on every part of the shoulder and around, then tighten from under the bone immediately, and turn the bandage onto the plaster, and wrap the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain so.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he be handled little by little, until the limbs are comforted, because he will heal more quickly; and then handle him more after five days or seven, and move him; and if he is firm and not softened, he is cured.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen due to moisture that has occurred, or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cauterization at three wounds, as he is placed in front of or on the cautery table.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven days he still cannot bear up with one arm above it, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and know that the joint can never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs near the elbow and kneecap or at the back, if it is done by force and stretching of hands, and another joint is used to treat it; and care is taken until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes gout in the limb and slow movement, if the patient uses bathing many times, until that gout is relieved, and returns to its first state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of a dislocation with a cut.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	It is said that the joint of the elbow is dislocated at multiple points, and then it returns; and if it has been dislocated in all directions, both front and back, and dislocations are not cured because they are clearly seen and felt; and each dislocation occurs according to its shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with the healthy one, so you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joined limb is weak, and it cannot move the arm, nor can it touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it so that the abscesses come out when they are alive, for if they came out while it was still inside, it would be more pain to get it out; and by chance it may not be able to be set again at all, especially when it's behind; this is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance one may die.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if the restoration is done, when it is such that it can be returned to its normal state, then you stretch out both hands towards your two hands; spread his arms and extend his hands so that they are drawn back according to the cut in all directions, upwards and downwards, and put the joint back into its socket or at the root of his palm, until he returns to his place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is a dislocation, so that it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and proudly from the base of the palm, which is loosened.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to the place, then perform great extension; and when two ministers extend the arm, and each of them tie up the arm, so that it does not move at extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have stretched a double cloth long and wide; and when the joint moves to join the joint to the hand, grasp any oil for softening the joint, then break the joint, until it returns; and when it is in its place, put on an emplastrure of pure wax with some olive oil, and bind the strain, and bend the arm onto the neck of the sick person, and let it rest for a few days, then set it free.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, let go of the ligament, and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not compress well, reapply the plaster and the ligament, and let it be for some days, until it is firmly set; then let it go.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels great pain after the setting of the joint, and it is quiet, then bathe him well and rub him thoroughly, and press until he is relaxed; or you put on the joint a fat mutton shank, then let it be for one day and one night, then take out the bone, and let him enter into the bath; and when he sweats, then rub the joint temperately, then put back the mutton shank, and then enter into the bath; and thus do two or three times until he is cured; and if you see, then apply warm moist fumigation with butter on the strained area, and press thereupon; then it will return to its original position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joints of the hand dislocate, and the return is lighter than the others. Whenever it happens again, you must bring it back to its place immediately, in the same way that it was displaced, so that the joint is swollen or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the remedy is that you put the patient's hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of the other hand, and straighten the wrist, so that it puts its palm on the appearance of the joint. And apply pressure until it returns to normal.
