Whenever this happens again, you must examine whether it has returned to its place; then put the patient's back on a table at extension and at resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if a dislocation is at the back of the hand, he instructs the patient to place his back against the table, and he places his hand above this appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	But if it returns now, then it is good if the straining of applying poultices calms abscesses and he allows him to resume in that sense.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	But if he cannot suffer it and you cannot put him to bed after some days, the joint will turn and he is hindered from nothing except until his hands are swollen and he cannot strain anything: then know that the nerves have been struck or the arteries; for there is no other remedy except by cauterizing near the case, and perhaps that does not bring any better thing.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hands are at rest, put on the plaster that we have said, then strain it and leave for four days, then remove it and let it be so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	But if it cannot move well and there is no discomfort, put the poultice of hot water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the joint in the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never have the joint of the hand dislocated on one side, nor on the back of the palm or stomach; so it is straight, and break the dislocation in your pouches as long as it revives, then support the head of the dislocated joint, and turn it towards the part where it is separated; and let it stay for two days, and then set it equal to that day; and do not bind it, if we have said so, and break it off one day, and make it move, and tie the nut; and do this often, as long as it is tight, and just as you did before, if it has dislocated on the stomach of the hand; and do it in the same way, whenever it is dislocated on another part.

Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne. And if she does not return by this cure, then take a table of three arms long, and chop under the skin, and the patient be on his side, and pour the head of the table under the skin, then put the middle of the table on the spine; and put your hands on the other head of the table, and press well, until he returns to the left; and if you see, do it to the turnip which turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then you put two stakes on the top of the patient’s head with one arm long, and between each stake, and above as well as below, one palm of a long inch space; and in each stake there should be one wound, or the turnip turns, and they are firmly stuck in the ground so that they do not move; between two stakes there should be one turnip, since the turnips that lie together turn, and there are two turnips an inch wide for turning the turnip; and then tie the strap that is between the creaks to the top of the turnip, and the other strap to the feet of the other turnip, and each of the servants makes his turnip turn with all the strain, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.

des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the knee
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Weaves that the joints of the knee and shoulder only come from dislocations, not from other joint issues; and the joint of the knee is displaced in four parts: within and outside, front and rear; and closer to it, and less so in front and rear.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of knee dislocations is that when you join a diseased leg to a healthy one, it becomes longer, and the patient's knees are more exposed than those of the healthy person; and they cannot double their knee movement by fire; and it is the ones who are located near the inflamed abscess, because the head of the dislocated shoulder comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of that which happens to the forelimb, it is that this accident is contrary to what happens behind.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who suffers thus before it happens to him, are that he stands well with his leg according to completion; all see this, do not double bend his knees in pain, and if you want him to walk, he cannot do so beforehand, retains his urine, and swells his groin, and when he goes, passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who suffers thus behind it happens to him, are that he cannot expand his knees, nor bend them, and is that leg more twisted than the other, and his groin is softened, and is the head of the crotch at the level below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation, are that if you return to the earlier state of dislocation, and it lingers according to its disposition, if there is no cure; and it is not wise to presume.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And when it comes to dislocations that are fresh, and there are four kinds of dislocation, hasten so you return the joint, and stretch it inwards and forwards, and move the arm on both sides; by chance if it returns, and there is no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, you should wish to have a strong minister, and strengthen the leg with two arms, or bind one of the joints above the knee; and there are other ministers who extend their hand upwards in that manner so they pour water from above onto their legs below, then bind it with a strong rope on the belly; and others tie the head to the joint; and stretch up and down all at once, until the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four forms, and if dislocation has occurred, as we have said, it is true.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If that is not the case, it is necessary to apply treatment to its form When the dislocation is in the pelvis, it is necessary to lift the patient on his healthy side, then tie him with a strip at the root of the scrotum, and the one below the angle, then stretch the strip upwards towards the angle, and towards the pubic bone; then take hold of other assistants' arms, and embrace the large strip of the sick scrotum, and extend it outwards in form: if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you cannot compress it in the manner we have said, it is necessary to tie the two feet of the sick together with a strong strip on both heels and knees; then let the leg be extended twice as much as the others; then hang them over the chief of a rope, and above the ground two long arms; then command one minister to embrace the head of the scrotum, and let other assistants hang alongside with the sick man, who will form an embrace: for the joint now returns quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation. S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, put on the same kind of bed, as we have said in the one with the gout, and givest to the sick on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when dislocations occur in front of you, it is fitting to stretch the ill limb immediately, and according to what I have said; and place the mirrors on the pain of being above the afflicted joint, then press with your other hand, and extend the arm towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocations are in front of you, it is not fitting to stretch the ill limb afterwards, nor to lift him up from the ground, but rather to make him as he was before being dislocated, just as we have said when coming down on the two hocks; and be on his face, and the ligament extended as we have said previously, and must press firmly on the joint at the table; and it will come to pass that the ill patient extends his legs, and they become even; then add the cauldron, and place the poultice, and the strain of a bandage, so that the hock does not move; and he must rest for three days or four, then he is released, and places on the poultice again; and if you see that they are even, you must apply the same strain as before, and leave him for three days; then release him, and let him walk well, until the members become comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joint is displaced in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and behind; but not forward.

des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, it is advisable to stretch them properly with work, and it is a light thing.

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wounds come with dislocation, and you try to restore it, many times the patients die; do not be presumptuous in your treatment, unless you are wise in the art and have used it for a long time, and unless you are pitiful, merciful, and patient; and do not harden. Use soothing remedies at first to treat abscesses, and let the patient be in God's hands, if you do not see any hope of recovery; and when you see hope, now restore the limb as it comes alive; and when the limb is restored, administer soothing remedies again, and cure the wound as it seems fitting, with ointments for dry wounds; and if there is a break with fractured bones, and small bones are exposed, set the bones, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, because this will cost you nothing but according to your Creator, and for the wisdom that has armed you and your body.
Amen	Amen.
